Timing Conditions for Seller's Claim of Lineage
Ruling on when seller's claim is accepted based on birth timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for when a seller's claim of lineage is accepted or rejected based on the timing of birth, and distinguish the consequences for the sale and the status of the slave-girl.

Core Idea
A seller's claim of lineage is rejected if the child is born after six months; only the buyer's confirmation can overcome this.

When a man sells a pregnant slave-girl and later claims the child, the timing of birth determines the validity of his claim. This lesson explores the Hanafi position: the seller's claim is tested against the minimum and maximum pregnancy durations (6 months and 2 years). Understanding these rules is essential for rulings on lineage, sale validity, and the mother's status as umm walad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two time thresholds
The passage specifies two critical periods: 6 months (minimum pregnancy) and 2 years (maximum pregnancy). These thresholds determine whether conception could have occurred during the seller's ownership.
These thresholds are based on Quranic and prophetic evidence, though not cited here.
2
Determine the default ruling for each threshold
If the child is born before 6 months (i.e., within 6 months from sale), the seller's claim is rejected because conception may have occurred after the sale. If born after 2 years, the claim is also rejected because conception cannot be certainly attributed to his ownership.
In both cases, the buyer's confirmation can change the outcome.
3
Analyse the effect of buyer confirmation
If the buyer confirms the seller's claim, lineage is established in both cases. However, the consequences differ: for birth within 6 months, the sale is void and the mother becomes umm walad; for birth after 2 years, the sale remains valid and the mother does not become umm walad.
The difference hinges on certainty: within 6 months, conception could have been before sale; after 2 years, it certainly was not.
4
Compare consequences for the sale and umm walad status
When birth occurs within 6 months and buyer confirms, the sale is void (because conception traces to before sale) and the mother becomes umm walad. When birth occurs after 2 years and buyer confirms, the sale is not void (because conception definitely after sale) and the mother does not become umm walad; she is only umm walad by nikah.
The term 'umm walad' here refers to the status as mother of a child from the owner, which entails certain rights.
5
Summarise the overall rule
The seller's claim is always rejected without buyer confirmation if the birth occurs after 6 months from sale. The distinction between the two windows (within 2 years vs. after 2 years) only matters when the buyer confirms: in the first window, the sale is rescinded; in the second, it is not.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of balancing probability and certainty in lineage claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأكثر يصدقه المشتري: [فحينئذ يثبت النسب ويبطل بيع الأمة والولد حر والأمة أم ولده. (ط)] أي إن ولدت الأمة من ستة أشهر من وقت البيع، ردت دعوة البائع؛ لاحتمال العلوق بعد البيع، فلم يوجد المصحح فيه بيقين إلا أن يصدق المشتري البائع، فحينئذ يثبت نسبه؛ لتصادقهما فيه، وتصير الأمة أم ولد له تبعاً للولد، ويبطل البيع؛ لاستناد العلوق إلى ما قبل البيع؛ لإمكانه، ولو ولدت لأكثر من سنتين من وقت البيع، لم تصح دعوة البائع؛ إذ لم يوجد اتصال العلوق بملكه يقيناً، وإن صدقه المشتري يثبت النسب؛ إذ عدم ثبوته لرعاية حقه، وإن صدقه زال ذلك المانع، ولم يبطل بيعه للجزم بأن العلوق ليس في ملكه فلا يثبت حقيقة العتق ولا حقه؛ لأنه دعوة تحرير، وغير المالك ليس من أهله، وكانت أم ولده نكاحاً. والحاصل أن رد الدعوى فيما إذا جاءت به لأكثر من ستة أشهر، و لم يصدقه المشتري، لا فرق فيه بين ما إذا جاءت به لأقل من سنتين أو لأكثر ، وإنما الفرق بينهما من جهة ثبوت الاستيلاد للأم بعد التصديق، ونقض البيع فيها، ورد الثمن (عيني، فتح)
'For more than that, the buyer confirms him': then lineage is established and the sale of the slave-girl is void, and the child is free and the slave-girl is his umm walad. (T) That is, if the slave-girl gives birth less than six months from the time of the sale, the seller's claim is rejected due to the possibility of conception after the sale, so there is no certain basis for it, unless the buyer confirms the seller, then his lineage is established due to their mutual confirmation, and the slave-girl becomes his umm walad following the child, and the sale is void because the conception can be traced to before the sale. And if she gives birth more than two years from the time of the sale, the seller's claim is not valid because there is no certain connection of conception to his ownership, but if the buyer confirms him, the lineage is established because its failure is due to protection of the buyer's right; if he confirms, that impediment is removed, but his sale is not void because it is certain that the conception was not in his ownership, so neither the reality of freedom nor his right is established, because it is a claim of tahrir, and a non-owner is not qualified for it, and she was his umm walad by marriage. The summary is that the rejection of the claim when she gives birth after more than six months and the buyer does not confirm him, there is no difference between whether she gives birth in less than two years or more. The difference between them is only regarding the establishment of istilad for the mother after confirmation, and the rescission of the sale in her case, and the return of the price. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage explains the timing conditions for the seller's claim of lineage. The key rule: if the slave-girl gives birth within six months of the sale, the seller's claim is rejected because the conception could have occurred after the sale. However, if the buyer confirms the claim, then lineage is established, the sale is void, and the mother becomes umm walad. If the birth occurs after more than two years, the seller's claim is also rejected because conception cannot be attributed to his ownership with certainty. If the buyer confirms, lineage is established but the sale is not void because the conception was certainly not during the seller's ownership, so the mother does not become umm walad. The difference between the two windows (less than two years vs. more than two years) only matters when the buyer confirms: in the first, the sale is void and the mother becomes umm walad; in the second, the sale remains valid and the mother does not become umm walad. In both, if the buyer does not confirm, the seller's claim is rejected. This shows the Hanafi approach to balancing probability and certainty in lineage claims.

Key Terms
ستة أشهر (sittat ashhur): The minimum period of pregnancy used to determine if conception likely occurred before or after sale.
سنتين (sanatayn): The maximum period of pregnancy according to the Hanafi school; after two years, conception is definitely not from the seller.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The seller's claim of lineage is only accepted with buyer confirmation if the child is born within the minimum and maximum pregnancy limits; without confirmation, the claim is always rejected.

Claiming Lineage of Twins and Effect of Sale
Ruling that claiming one twin establishes lineage for both and invalidates buyer's freeing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on claiming lineage of twins and apply the rule to determine the validity of a prior sale and freeing.

Core Idea
Twins are legally one unit: establishing lineage of one establishes lineage of both, overriding prior transactions.

In Hanafi family law, twins are treated as a single legal entity due to their shared conception. This lesson explores the effect of a seller's claim of lineage on the status of twin children, especially when one has been sold and freed. The key is the principle of 'one water' (ma' wahid), which creates an inseparable legal bond.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (claiming lineage of twins) and the resulting legal effect (invalidity of buyer's freeing).
The ruling is not about the validity of the claim itself but its consequence on prior transactions.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
Identify the proof: the twins are created from one water (ma' wahid), establishing a necessary link between them.
This is a dalil 'aqli (rational proof) based on physical fact.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? Because if lineage of one is established, the other must share it, making them both free from origin.
The impossibility of one being free and the other a slave from the same conception.
4
Note the Exception (Single Child)
Compare with the case of a single child: the seller's claim does not invalidate the buyer's freeing because that would nullify the purpose of manumission.
This exception shows that the twin rule is based on the specific illa of shared origin.
5
Apply the Qiyas Structure
The text uses qiyas: asl (single child – freeing not invalidated), far' (twins), illa (shared water), hukm (freeing invalidated).
The illa is jaliyyah (evident), and the extraction method is tahqiq al-manat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التوأمين وهما ولدان بين ولادتيهما أقل من ستة أشهر. (ط) ثبت نسبهما منه لأنهما خلقا من ماء واحد فثبوت نسب أحدهما يستلزم ثبوت نسب الآخر، وإنما يعرف أنهما توأمان إذا كان بين ولادتيهما أقل من ستة أشهر، وإن كان بينهما ستة أشهر فصاعداً، فليسا بتوأمين؛ لأن أقل مدة الحمل ستة أشهر، فإذا أتت بولد ثم بولد آخر لأقل من ستة أشهر يعلم بالضرورة أنهما من ماء واحد. رمز الحقائق: ۲۱۲/۲] (فتح) وأعتقه المشتري: ثم ادعى البائع بعده أنه ابنه ثبت نسبهما منه. (عيني) بطل عتق المشتري: أي إذا ولدت أمة رجل توأمين ثم باع الرجل أحدهما وأعتقه المشتري، ثم ادعى البائع نسياً الآخر، بطل عتق المشتري وثبت نسبهما منه، وجه بطلان العتق: أن دعوى البائع بعده صحت في الذي لم يبعه، ولمن ضرورة ذلك ثبوت نسب الآخر؛ لأنهما من ماء واحد فيلزم منه بطلان عتق المشتري؛ لكونهما حري الأصل؛ إذ يستحيل أن يكون أحدهما حرّ الأصل، والآخر رقيقاً، وهما من ماء واحد بخلاف ما إذا كان الولد واحداً، فباعه المالك وأعتقه المشتري، حيث لا يبطل فيه إعتاق المشتري، بدعوى البائع نسبه؛ لأن العتق لو بطل فيه بطل المقصود؛
The twins: they are two children between whose births there is less than six months. (T) Their lineage is established from him because they were created from one water; so the establishment of lineage of one necessitates the establishment of lineage of the other. They are known to be twins only if the time between their births is less than six months; if it is six months or more, they are not twins because the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months. So if she gives birth to a child and then another child in less than six months, it is known by necessity that they are from one water. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 212/2] (Fath) 'And the buyer freed him': then the seller claimed after that that he was his son, so their lineage is established from him. (Ayni) 'The freeing of the buyer is void': i.e., if a man's slave-girl gives birth to twins, then the man sells one of them and the buyer frees him, then the seller claims the lineage of the other (the unsold), the buyer's freeing is void and their lineage from him is established. The reason for the invalidity of the freeing: that the seller's claim afterward is valid regarding the one he did not sell, and by necessity the lineage of the other is established because they are from one water, which entails the invalidity of the buyer's freeing, because they are both free from the origin; it is impossible that one is free from the origin and the other is a slave, while they are from one water. Unlike the case when the child is one, the owner sells him and the buyer frees him, where the freeing is not invalidated by the seller's claim of his lineage, because if the freeing were invalidated, the purpose (of freeing) would be nullified.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage deals with claims of lineage for twins. The key rule is that if a person claims lineage for one twin, the other twin automatically shares that lineage because they are from one water (conceived from the same act). Twins are identified by the time between births being less than six months; if it is six months or more, they are not considered twins. If a seller sells one of the twins and the buyer frees him, then later the seller claims the other twin as his son, the buyer's freeing of the first twin is invalidated. The reason is that both twins must share the same status; it is impossible for one to be free from origin and the other a slave. However, if there is only one child, the seller's claim does not invalidate the buyer's freeing, because otherwise the purpose of manumission would be lost. This shows the Hanafi principle of legal causation based on the physical unity of twins.

Key Terms
توأمين (taw'amayn): Two children born from the same pregnancy with less than six months between their births.
ماء واحد (ma' wahid): A single seminal emission; the basis for legal unity between twins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man sells one of twin children born to his slave-girl and the buyer frees him, and then the seller claims lineage of the other twin, what happens to the buyer's freeing?
A) It remains valid, and the freed child is free.
B) It is invalidated because both twins share the same lineage and status.
C) The buyer must free the other twin as well.
D) The seller must compensate the buyer.

Key Takeaway
Twins are legally inseparable: claiming lineage of one automatically establishes lineage of the other, overriding prior transactions like sale and freeing.

Child Claimed by Both Spouses
Ruling on a child claimed by both husband and wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when both spouses claim a child from different relationships and identify the condition that changes the ruling.

Core Idea
When both spouses claim a child, the child is attributed to both until he can speak; then his word decides.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents a concise rule on disputed lineage when a child is in the custody of both spouses. The default presumption (al-‘amm) is that the child belongs to both, because each spouse's claim is equally strong due to the marital bed (firash) and physical custody. However, if the child is old enough to express himself coherently (mu‘abbir), his statement is given weight, and he is attributed to the parent he confirms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
Both spouses claim the child as their own from different previous relationships.
The child is in the physical custody (yad) of both.
2
Determine the child's ability to speak
If the child is ghayr mu‘abbir (cannot express coherently), apply the default ruling.
ghayr mu‘abbir means a child who cannot articulate a clear statement.
3
Apply the default ruling
The child is considered the son of both spouses.
This is the ‘amm (prevailing view) cited in the text.
4
Identify the exception
If the child is mu‘abbir (can speak coherently), his word is accepted.
The child belongs to whichever parent he confirms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان صبي في يد زوجين فالعام أنه ابنه من غيرها، وزعمت هذه الزوجة أنه ابنها من غيره، فهو ابنهما. هذا إذا كان الصبي غير معبر، وإلا فهو لمن صدقه.
And if there is a boy in the hands of two spouses, and the husband claims he is his son from another wife, and this wife claims he is her son from another husband, then he is the son of both. This is if the boy cannot express himself; otherwise, he belongs to whomever he confirms.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on a disputed claim of lineage when a child is in the custody of both a husband and wife. Both claim the child as their own from different previous relationships. Since both have equal physical custody (yad) and the marital bed (firash) is a strong indicator, the child is considered the son of both parents. If the child is old enough to speak coherently (mu'abbir), his word is accepted, and he may choose which parent to affiliate with.

Key Terms
عام (al-‘amm): The general presumption (zahir) or prevailing opinion.
غير معبر (ghayr mu‘abbir): A child who cannot clearly express himself or articulate a coherent statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When both spouses claim a child as their own from different relationships, what is the ruling if the child cannot express himself?
A) The child belongs to the husband only
B) The child belongs to the wife only
C) The child is considered the son of both
D) The child is free (not affiliated to either)

Key Takeaway
A child in joint custody claimed by both spouses is attributed to both unless the child can speak clearly and choose a parent.

Scope of a Man's Iqrar for Relatives
List of valid iqrar types for a man

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of relatives for whom a man's iqrar is valid and identify the specific conditions for wife and client.

Core Idea
A man's iqrar is valid only for four: father, son, wife, and client of emancipation.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage, where the author lists the valid types of iqrar for a man. The sick person's acknowledgment is treated with caution, but here it is deemed valid because it imposes only on himself. The four categories are defined, and each has its own conditions to prevent fraud or conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
From the text, list the four: father, son, wife, and client of emancipation (mawla al-`itaqah). Note that 'father' includes mother according to some narrations.
The passage mentions a disagreement in sources about including the mother; the matn includes the mother, but al-Mabsut lists only father.
2
Analyze the condition for the wife
The wife must not be in another's marriage or iddah, not be a sister of the acknowledger's existing wife, not be a fourth wife, and not be a Magian or idolater.
These conditions ensure no conflict with existing marriage rules.
3
Analyze the condition for the client
The client must not have his wala' already established from another. The acknowledger must say 'this is my freedman' (mu'tiq if lower, mu'taq if higher).
Wala' is the relationship of clientage; once established, it cannot be reassigned.
4
State the ruling's hukm level
The iqrar is sahih (valid) if conditions are met. It is a binding acknowledgment on the acknowledger.
It is not a contract but an admission that creates legal consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح إقراره لأنه إقرار على نفسه، وليس فيه حمل النسب على الغير، وشروطه ما بينا في الابن وأعاد صحة الإقرار بالولد؛ لذكر جملة ما يصح في جانب الرجل، وأفاد بالصراحة صحة الإقرار بالأم، وهو رواية "تحفة الفقهاء" و"شرح الفرائض"، والمذكور في "المبسوط": أن إقرار الرجل يصح بأربعة بالأب والابن والمرأة ومولى العتاقة.  ٦٧ كتاب الإقرار أحكام إقرار المريض بالولد والوالدين والزوجة والمولى، وإقرارها بالوالدين والزوج والمولى وبالولد إن شهدت قابلة أو صدقها زوجها ولابد من تصديق هؤلاء، وصح التصديق بعد موت المقر إلا تصديق الزوج بعد موتها،. بالزوجة أي تصديق هولاء بالولد بأن قال لآخر : هذا ولدي (معدن) والوالدين بأن قال لرجل هذا أبي ولامرأة: هذه أمي. (معدن) والزوجة بأن قال لامرأة هذه زوجتي. (عيني) وبالولد إن شهدت قابلة [أي وصح إقرارها بالولد بأن قالت هذا ولدي (معدن، عيني)] أي وصح إقرار المرأة بالولد بأحد الشرطين: الأول: أن تشهد قابلة أو غيرها بولادته منها؛ ليتعين الولد والثاني: أن يصدقها زوجها، وكانت ذات زوج أو معتدة، وادعت أن الولد منه؛ لأن فيه تحميل النسب على الزوج، فلا يلزم بقولها؛ لأن النسب بالفراش والحق للزوج، فإذا صدقها زوجها فقد أقر به، وأما إذا لم يكن لها زوج ولا هي معتدة، أو كان لها زوج وادعت أن الولد من غيره صح إقرارها؛ لأن فيه إلزاما على نفسها دون غيرها، فينفذ عليها. (عيني، فتح) ولابد من تصديق هؤلاء [يعني تصديق الولد والوالدين والزوجة والمولى والزوج. (عيني)] أي إنما يصح الإقرار إذا صدق المقر له في الإقرار في المسائل كلها؛ لأن إقرار غيرهم لا يلزمهم؛ لأن كلاً منهم في يد نفسه إلا إذا كان المقر له صغيراً لا يعبر عن نفسه، أو عبداً له فيثبت نسبه بمجرد الإقرار، ولو كان عبداً لغيره يشترط تصديق مولاه. (عيني، فتح) وصح التصديق أي صح تصديق المقر له من هؤلاء المذكورين بعد موت المقر؛ لبقاء النسب بعد موت المقر، وإن أقر بنكاحها فصدقته بعد موته صح حتى يكون لها الميراث والمهر؛ لبقاء حكم النكاح، وهو العدة، فإنها آثار النكاح، ولهذا جاز لها غسله كما في حالة الحياة ميتاً. إلا تصديق الزوج إلخ: أي إذا أقرت المرأة بالزوج، فصدقها الزوج بعد موتها، فإنه لا يصح؛ لانقطاع النكاح بعد موت المرأة عند أبي حنيفة، وأما إذا أقر الزوج بالزوجة وصدقت المرأة بعد موت الزوج، فإنه لا تصح بالاتفاق، وعندهما يجوز تصديق الزوج بعد موت الزوجة؛ لبقاء النكاح بعد موت المرأة في حق الإرث والإقرار قائم؛ لأن التكذيب منه لم يوجد، فصح التصديق بعد موتها، فيثبت النكاح بتصادقهما، فيرث منها، ولهذا لو أقام البينة على النكاح بعد موتها، تقبل، وله: أنها لما ماتت زال النكاح بعلائقه، حتى يجوز له أن يتزوج أختها، وأربعا سواها، ولا يحل له أن يغسلها، فبطل إقرارها، =
His acknowledgment is valid because it is an acknowledgment against himself, and it does not involve imposing lineage on others. Its conditions are what we explained regarding the son. He repeated the validity of acknowledgment of the child to list what is valid on the man's side, and he explicitly indicated the validity of acknowledgment of the mother, which is a narration in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' and Sharh al-Fara'id, and it is mentioned in al-Mabsut that a man's acknowledgment is valid for four: father, son, wife, and client of emancipation. [Page 68] Book of Acknowledgment: Rulings of the sick person's acknowledgment of child, parents, wife, and client, and her acknowledgment of parents, husband, and client, and of a child if a midwife testifies or her husband confirms her. It is necessary that these persons confirm. The confirmation is valid after the death of the acknowledger except the husband's confirmation after her death. 'The wife' means these persons' confirmation: regarding the child, by saying to another: 'This is my child'; regarding parents, by saying to a man: 'This is my father' and to a woman: 'This is my mother'; regarding the wife, by saying to a woman: 'This is my wife.' That is, his acknowledgment of a wife is valid if the woman is free from another's marriage and its waiting period, and that under the acknowledger there is not her sister, nor four other women besides her, and that she is not a Magian or an idolater. 'The client' means the client of emancipation, whether he is the manumitter (mu'tiq) or the manumitted (mu'taq), for acknowledgment of each is valid. That is, the higher and lower, by saying: 'This is my freedman' if his wala' is not already established from another. Her acknowledgment is also valid. The client, because it does not involve imposing lineage on others, so it is accepted. Regarding the child, if a midwife testifies — i.e., her acknowledgment of a child is valid if she says 'This is my child' with one of two conditions: first, that a midwife or other testifies to its birth from her to establish the child; second, that her husband confirms, if she has a husband or is in waiting period, and she claims the child is from him, because it involves placing lineage on the husband, so it is not binding by her word alone, because lineage is by marriage and the right belongs to the husband; if her husband confirms her, he has acknowledged it. But if she has no husband nor waiting period, or has a husband and claims the child from someone else, her acknowledgment is valid because it imposes only on herself, so it is binding on her. It is necessary that these persons confirm — meaning the child, parents, wife, client, and husband. That is, the acknowledgment is valid only if the acknowledged person confirms it in all these matters, because the acknowledgment of others is not binding on them, since each is in control of himself, except if the acknowledged is a minor who cannot express himself, or his own slave, then his lineage is established by mere acknowledgment. If it is a slave belonging to another, the confirmation of his master is required. The confirmation is valid after the death of the acknowledger because the lineage remains after the death of the acknowledger. If he acknowledges marriage and she confirms after his death, it is valid so that she receives inheritance and dower, because the ruling of marriage remains, which is the waiting period, for it is the effects of marriage, and therefore it is permissible for her to wash him as in life. Except for the husband's confirmation etc.: if a woman acknowledges a husband and the husband confirms after her death, it is not valid because marriage ends after the woman's death according to Abu Hanifa. As for if the husband acknowledges a wife and the woman confirms after the husband's death, that is not valid by agreement. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the husband's confirmation after the wife's death is valid because the marriage remains after the woman's death regarding inheritance, and the acknowledgment stands because his denial did not occur; so the confirmation after her death is valid, and the marriage is established by their mutual acknowledgment, so he inherits from her. This is why if he brings evidence of marriage after her death, it is accepted. His argument is that when she died, the marriage and its connections ceased, so it is permissible for him to marry her sister and four others besides her, and he is not permitted to wash her, so her acknowledgment is void.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage covers the scope of valid iqrar for a sick person. First, it reiterates that a man's iqrar is valid for four categories: father, son, wife, and client of emancipation. Each has conditions: for the wife, she must not be married to another, not be within her iddah, and not be a sister of his existing wife, nor a Magian or idolater. For the client, his wala' must not be already established. Then it discusses a woman's iqrar: she can acknowledge parents, husband, client, and child under conditions. For the child, she needs either a midwife's testimony of birth or her husband's confirmation (if she claims the child from him). The necessity of confirmation (tasdiq) by the acknowledged person is emphasized: for the iqrar to be binding on them, they must confirm, except when the acknowledged is a minor or a slave of the acknowledger. Confirmation can occur after the death of the acknowledger, except for the husband's confirmation after the wife's death according to Abu Hanifa, due to the marriage being completely severed. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ, allowing it because the marriage remains for inheritance purposes.

Key Terms
مولى العتاقة (mawla al-`itaqah): Client of emancipation, either the master (mu'tiq) or the freed slave (mu'taq).
عدة (iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death, during which a woman cannot remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She must be Muslim
B) She must be free of another's marriage and iddah
C) She must be younger than him
D) She must have witnesses

Key Takeaway
A man's iqrar is only valid for father, son, wife, and client of emancipation, each with specific conditions to prevent fraud.

Woman's Iqrar for a Child: Conditions of Midwife or Husband Confirmation
Rules for woman's iqrar of a child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required for a woman's iqrar of a child to impose lineage on her husband, and explain when her iqrar is binding on herself alone.

Core Idea
A woman's iqrar of a child binds the husband only if he confirms or a midwife testifies.

This lesson addresses the specific rules for a woman's iqrar of a child. Unlike iqrar of other relationships, a child's lineage affects the father, so extra safeguards are needed. The passage lists two ways to make the iqrar effective against the husband: a midwife's testimony of birth, or the husband's own confirmation. If neither is present, the iqrar may still bind the woman herself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule for woman's iqrar
A woman's iqrar is valid for parents, husband, and client because it only affects herself. For a child, it is different.
Her iqrar of a child is valid but may not impose lineage on the husband.
2
Isolate the two conditions for child iqrar affecting husband
Condition 1: A midwife (or other woman) testifies to the birth. Condition 2: The husband confirms her claim that the child is from him.
Both conditions serve to prevent fraudulent imposition of lineage.
3
Analyze scenarios where conditions are absent
If she has no husband or claims the child is from someone else, her iqrar is valid and binding on herself to establish lineage to her.
The child's lineage to her is established by her statement alone.
4
Determine the ruling when she claims the child from the husband but he denies
The iqrar is not binding on the husband; his denial suffices. The child is only attributed to the mother.
Lineage is by marriage (firash), not by mere claim.

(معدن)] أي صح إقراره بالزوجة إذا كانت المرأة خالية عن نكاح الغير وعدته، وأن لا يكون تحت المقر أختها، ولا أربع نسوة سواها، وأن لا تكون مجوسية ولا وثنية. والمولى [أي مولى العتاقة سواء كان معتقاً بالكسر أو معتقاً بالفتح، فإن الإقرار بكل واحد منهما صحيح. (عيني)] أي الأعلى والأسفل بأن قال: هذا معتقي إذا لم يكن ولاؤه ثابتاً من الغير. (عناية فتح وإقرارها أي وصح إقرار المرأة أيضاً. (عيني) والمولى لأنه ليس فيه حمل النسب على غيرها، فيقبل. (عيني) وبالولد إن شهدت قابلة [أي وصح إقرارها بالولد بأن قالت هذا ولدي (معدن، عيني)] أي وصح إقرار المرأة بالولد بأحد الشرطين: الأول: أن تشهد قابلة أو غيرها بولادته منها؛ ليتعين الولد والثاني: أن يصدقها زوجها، وكانت ذات زوج أو معتدة، وادعت أن الولد منه؛ لأن فيه تحميل النسب على الزوج، فلا يلزم بقولها؛ لأن النسب بالفراش والحق للزوج، فإذا صدقها زوجها فقد أقر به، وأما إذا لم يكن لها زوج ولا هي معتدة، أو كان لها زوج وادعت أن الولد من غيره صح إقرارها؛ لأن فيه إلزاما على نفسها دون غيرها، فينفذ عليها. (عيني، فتح) ولابد من تصديق هؤلاء [يعني تصديق الولد والوالدين والزوجة والمولى والزوج. (عيني)] أي إنما يصح الإقرار إذا صدق المقر له في الإقرار في المسائل كلها؛ لأن إقرار غيرهم لا يلزمهم؛ لأن كلاً منهم في يد نفسه إلا إذا كان المقر له صغيراً لا يعبر عن نفسه، أو عبداً له فيثبت نسبه بمجرد الإقرار، ولو كان عبداً لغيره يشترط تصديق مولاه. (عيني، فتح) وصح التصديق أي صح تصديق المقر له من هؤلاء المذكورين بعد موت المقر؛ لبقاء النسب بعد موت المقر، وإن أقر بنكاحها فصدقته بعد موته صح حتى يكون لها الميراث والمهر؛ لبقاء حكم النكاح، وهو العدة، فإنها آثار النكاح، ولهذا جاز لها غسله كما في حالة الحياة ميتاً. إلا تصديق الزوج إلخ: أي إذا أقرت المرأة بالزوج، فصدقها الزوج بعد موتها، فإنه لا يصح؛ لانقطاع النكاح بعد موت المرأة عند أبي حنيفة، وأما إذا أقر الزوج بالزوجة وصدقت المرأة بعد موت الزوج، فإنه لا تصح بالاتفاق، وعندهما يجوز تصديق الزوج بعد موت الزوجة؛ لبقاء النكاح بعد موت المرأة في حق الإرث والإقرار قائم؛ لأن التكذيب منه لم يوجد، فصح التصديق بعد موتها، فيثبت النكاح بتصادقهما، فيرث منها، ولهذا لو أقام البينة على النكاح بعد موتها، تقبل، وله: أنها لما ماتت زال النكاح بعلائقه، حتى يجوز له أن يتزوج أختها، وأربعا سواها، ولا يحل له أن يغسلها، فبطل إقرارها، =
His acknowledgment is valid because it is an acknowledgment against himself, and it does not involve imposing lineage on others. Its conditions are what we explained regarding the son. He repeated the validity of acknowledgment of the child to list what is valid on the man's side, and he explicitly indicated the validity of acknowledgment of the mother, which is a narration in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' and Sharh al-Fara'id, and it is mentioned in al-Mabsut that a man's acknowledgment is valid for four: father, son, wife, and client of emancipation. [Page 68] Book of Acknowledgment: Rulings of the sick person's acknowledgment of child, parents, wife, and client, and her acknowledgment of parents, husband, and client, and of a child if a midwife testifies or her husband confirms her. It is necessary that these persons confirm. The confirmation is valid after the death of the acknowledger except the husband's confirmation after her death. 'The wife' means these persons' confirmation: regarding the child, by saying to another: 'This is my child'; regarding parents, by saying to a man: 'This is my father' and to a woman: 'This is my mother'; regarding the wife, by saying to a woman: 'This is my wife.' That is, his acknowledgment of a wife is valid if the woman is free from another's marriage and its waiting period, and that under the acknowledger there is not her sister, nor four other women besides her, and that she is not a Magian or an idolater. 'The client' means the client of emancipation, whether he is the manumitter (mu'tiq) or the manumitted (mu'taq), for acknowledgment of each is valid. That is, the higher and lower, by saying: 'This is my freedman' if his wala' is not already established from another. Her acknowledgment is also valid. The client, because it does not involve imposing lineage on others, so it is accepted. Regarding the child, if a midwife testifies — i.e., her acknowledgment of a child is valid if she says 'This is my child' with one of two conditions: first, that a midwife or other testifies to its birth from her to establish the child; second, that her husband confirms, if she has a husband or is in waiting period, and she claims the child is from him, because it involves placing lineage on the husband, so it is not binding by her word alone, because lineage is by marriage and the right belongs to the husband; if her husband confirms her, he has acknowledged it. But if she has no husband nor waiting period, or has a husband and claims the child from someone else, her acknowledgment is valid because it imposes only on herself, so it is binding on her. It is necessary that these persons confirm — meaning the child, parents, wife, client, and husband. That is, the acknowledgment is valid only if the acknowledged person confirms it in all these matters, because the acknowledgment of others is not binding on them, since each is in control of himself, except if the acknowledged is a minor who cannot express himself, or his own slave, then his lineage is established by mere acknowledgment. If it is a slave belonging to another, the confirmation of his master is required. The confirmation is valid after the death of the acknowledger because the lineage remains after the death of the acknowledger. If he acknowledges marriage and she confirms after his death, it is valid so that she receives inheritance and dower, because the ruling of marriage remains, which is the waiting period, for it is the effects of marriage, and therefore it is permissible for her to wash him as in life. Except for the husband's confirmation etc.: if a woman acknowledges a husband and the husband confirms after her death, it is not valid because marriage ends after the woman's death according to Abu Hanifa. As for if the husband acknowledges a wife and the woman confirms after the husband's death, that is not valid by agreement. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the husband's confirmation after the wife's death is valid because the marriage remains after the woman's death regarding inheritance, and the acknowledgment stands because his denial did not occur; so the confirmation after her death is valid, and the marriage is established by their mutual acknowledgment, so he inherits from her. This is why if he brings evidence of marriage after her death, it is accepted. His argument is that when she died, the marriage and its connections ceased, so it is permissible for him to marry her sister and four others besides her, and he is not permitted to wash her, so her acknowledgment is void.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage covers the scope of valid iqrar for a sick person. First, it reiterates that a man's iqrar is valid for four categories: father, son, wife, and client of emancipation. Each has conditions: for the wife, she must not be married to another, not be within her iddah, and not be a sister of his existing wife, nor a Magian or idolater. For the client, his wala' must not be already established. Then it discusses a woman's iqrar: she can acknowledge parents, husband, client, and child under conditions. For the child, she needs either a midwife's testimony of birth or her husband's confirmation (if she claims the child from him). The necessity of confirmation (tasdiq) by the acknowledged person is emphasized: for the iqrar to be binding on them, they must confirm, except when the acknowledged is a minor or a slave of the acknowledger. Confirmation can occur after the death of the acknowledger, except for the husband's confirmation after the wife's death according to Abu Hanifa, due to the marriage being completely severed. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ, allowing it because the marriage remains for inheritance purposes.

Key Terms
قابلة (qabilah): Midwife, whose testimony can establish birth for a woman's iqrar of a child.
فراش (firash): Marital bed; lineage is attributed to the husband of the mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman married to Zaid says 'this child is from Zaid.' Zaid denies. She brings a midwife who testifies to the birth. What is the ruling?
A) Child is attributed to Zaid
B) Child is attributed only to the woman
C) Iqrar is invalid
D) Requires DNA test

Key Takeaway
A woman's iqrar of a child binds her husband only if she has a midwife testify or he confirms; otherwise, it only establishes her own motherhood.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
12 min
Confirmation (Tasdiq) and the Dispute on Post-Death Confirmation by Husband
Rules of tasdiq and a specific ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that tasdiq is required for all iqrar except for minors and own slaves, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the husband's confirmation after the wife's death is valid.

Core Idea
Tasdiq (confirmation) is required for iqrar to bind the acknowledged, except for minors and slaves of the acknowledger.

The final part of the passage discusses the requirement of confirmation (tasdiq) by the acknowledged person. Generally, the iqrar is not binding on the other party until they confirm. Exceptions are made for minors and slaves of the acknowledger. The passage then delves into a specific dispute: when a woman acknowledges a husband and he confirms after her death. Abu Hanifa deems this invalid, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it valid.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule of tasdiq
For an iqrar to be binding on the acknowledged person, they must confirm (tasdiq). This applies to the child, parents, wife, client, and husband.
Without confirmation, the iqrar only binds the acknowledger himself.
2
Identify the exceptions to tasdiq
Exceptions: if the acknowledged is a minor (cannot express) or a slave of the acknowledger, then confirmation is not needed.
For a slave of another, the master's confirmation is required.
3
Analyze the timing of tasdiq
Tasdiq is valid even after the death of the acknowledger, except for one case: the husband's confirmation after the wife's death according to Abu Hanifa.
The general rule: lineage and marriage effects survive death.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa: husband's confirmation after wife's death invalid because marriage ends completely. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: valid because marriage continues for inheritance and iddah.
The text presents both views but seems to lean towards Abu Hanifa.

Source Text

Conditions for a Sick Person's Acknowledgment of a Spouse
Ruling statement with conditions for spouse acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for a valid acknowledgment of a spouse by a sick person and explain why each condition is required.

Core Idea
A sick person's acknowledgment of a spouse is valid only if the woman is free to marry and the man has capacity to marry her.

The Hanafi school recognizes a sick person's acknowledgment of a spouse as valid, but with careful conditions to prevent abuse and protect existing marriages. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explained in al-Hidayah, lists four specific conditions that must be met. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly applying the ruling in estate and family matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sick person's acknowledgment of a woman as his spouse. The ruling is that it is sahih (valid) only when all conditions are met.
Recall that iqrār is a binding declaration; it does not create a right but affirms an existing relationship.
2
List the four conditions for validity
The text explicitly states four conditions: the woman must not be married to another or in her 'iddah; the acknowledging person must not have her sister as a wife; he must not have four other wives besides her; and she must not be a Magian or idol worshipper.
These conditions ensure the acknowledgment does not conflict with existing marriage rights.
3
Understand the rationale behind each condition
Each condition prevents a specific conflict: (1) avoids bigamy, (2) avoids marrying sisters simultaneously, (3) respects the limit of four wives, (4) ensures the woman is eligible for marriage to a Muslim.
The fourth condition allows a Kitābiyya (People of the Book) since she is not a Magian or idol worshipper.
4
Distinguish spouse conditions from other acknowledgments
Unlike acknowledging a child or parent, the spouse acknowledgment requires specific conditions related to marriage capacity. The passage also notes that tasdiq (confirmation) by the acknowledged person is generally required.
For spouse, confirmation by the woman (tasdiq) is needed for full effect, except in certain cases after death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام إقرار المريض بالولد والوالدين والزوجة والمولى، وإقرارها بالوالدين والزوج والمولى وبالولد إن شهدت قابلة أو صدقها زوجها ولابد من تصديق هؤلاء، وصح التصديق بعد موت المقر إلا تصديق الزوج بعد موتها،. بالزوجة بأن قال لامرأة هذه زوجتي. (معدن)] أي صح إقراره بالزوجة إذا كانت المرأة خالية عن نكاح الغير وعدته، وأن لا يكون تحت المقر أختها، ولا أربع نسوة سواها، وأن لا تكون مجوسية ولا وثنية.
Rulings of the sick person's acknowledgment of child, parents, spouse, and master; and her acknowledgment of parents, husband, master, and child if a midwife testifies or her husband confirms her, and confirmation of these is necessary, and confirmation is valid after the death of the acknowledging person except the husband's confirmation after her death. Regarding spouse: that he says to a woman 'this is my wife' – meaning his acknowledgment of spouse is valid if the woman is free from marriage to another and from her waiting period, and that the acknowledging person does not have her sister under him, nor four other women besides her, and that she is not a Magian or idol worshipper.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Marghinani's Hidayah commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It opens by stating the general rule that a sick person may acknowledge a child, parents, spouse, and master, and a woman may acknowledge parents, husband, master, and child under certain conditions. The explanation then details the conditions for a valid acknowledgment of a spouse by a man. The conditions are: (1) the woman must not be married to another or in her 'iddah from another marriage; (2) the acknowledging man must not have her sister as a wife simultaneously; (3) he must not already have four wives besides her; (4) she must not be a Magian or idol worshipper. These conditions prevent conflict with existing marriages and ensure the woman is eligible for marriage. The passage also notes that confirmation (tasdiq) by the acknowledged person is required for validity, and confirmation after the death of the acknowledging person is generally valid except for the husband's confirmation after the wife's death, a point of ikhtilaf discussed later.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): A legal acknowledgment or confession by a person regarding a right or relationship, binding on the acknowledger.
تصديق (tasdiq): Confirmation or affirmation by the person in whose favor the acknowledgment is made, required for the acknowledgment to be effective against others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of a sick person's acknowledgment of a spouse?
A) The woman must not be married to another.
B) The woman must not be in her 'iddah from another.
C) The man must not have four wives besides her.
D) The woman must be a Kitābiyya (People of the Book).

Key Takeaway
A sick person's acknowledgment of a spouse is valid only when four specific conditions are met, preventing conflict with existing marriages and ensuring eligibility.

Acknowledgment of Master and Woman's Acknowledgment of Child
Explains validity and conditions for acknowledging a master and a woman acknowledging a child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's acknowledgment of a child is valid and distinguish when it binds the husband versus when it binds only herself.

Core Idea
A woman's word alone cannot impose lineage on her husband; proof is needed when another's right is at stake.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies two distinct types of acknowledgment: a master's acknowledgment of a freed slave, and a woman's acknowledgment of a child. The central legal insight is that the validity and effect of acknowledgment depend on whether it imposes obligations on others or only on oneself. Let's unpack the conditions and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two separate rulings in the text: acknowledgment of a master (mawlā) and a woman's acknowledgment of a child. Note the hukm level for each.
The master can be either the emancipator or the emancipated slave.
2
Analyze the master's acknowledgment
Understand that acknowledgment of a master is valid unconditionally, as long as the right of wala' is not already established from another source. This imposes no burden on others.
3
Analyze the woman's acknowledgment
Break down the conditions based on marital status. If she is married or in 'idda and claims the child from the husband, external proof (midwife testimony or husband's confirmation) is required. If she is not married or claims from someone else, her statement alone is binding on herself.
The key distinction is whether the acknowledgment imposes on the husband's right or only on herself.
4
Trace the ta'lil (reasoning)
The reasoning (qiyas) is that when acknowledgment imposes on others, it requires evidence to protect their rights. When it imposes only on oneself, one's own statement is sufficient.
This is the underlying legal principle that links the two rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمولى [ أي مولى العتاقة سواء كان معتقاً بالكسر أو معتقاً بالفتح، فإن الإقرار بكل واحد منهما صحيح. (عيني)] أي الأعلى والأسفل بأن قال: هذا معتقي إذا لم يكن ولاؤه ثابتاً من الغير. (عناية فتح وإقرارها أي وصح إقرار المرأة أيضاً. (عيني) والمولى لأنه ليس فيه حمل النسب على غيرها، فيقبل. (عيني) وبالولد إن شهدت قابلة [ أي وصح إقرارها بالولد بأن قالت هذا ولدي (معدن، عيني)] أي وصح إقرار المرأة بالولد بأحد الشرطين: الأول: أن تشهد قابلة أو غيرها بولادته منها؛ ليتعين الولد والثاني: أن يصدقها زوجها، وكانت ذات زوج أو معتدة، وادعت أن الولد منه؛ لأن فيه تحميل النسب على الزوج، فلا يلزم بقولها؛ لأن النسب بالفراش والحق للزوج، فإذا صدقها زوجها فقد أقر به، وأما إذا لم يكن لها زوج ولا هي معتدة، أو كان لها زوج وادعت أن الولد من غيره صح إقرارها؛ لأن فيه إلزاما على نفسها دون غيرها، فينفذ عليها. (عيني، فتح)
And the master – meaning the master of emancipation, whether he is the emancipator (mu'tiq) or the emancipated (mu'taq), so acknowledgment of each is valid. Meaning the higher and lower as he says: 'this is my emancipated slave' if his wala' is not already established from another. (Al-Inayah, Al-Fath) And her acknowledgment – meaning the woman's acknowledgment is also valid. (Al-Ayni) And the master because it does not involve attributing lineage to others, so it is accepted. (Al-Ayni) And regarding a child if a midwife testifies – meaning her acknowledgment of a child is valid if she says 'this is my child' (from Ma'din and Al-Ayni) – meaning the woman's acknowledgment of a child is valid under one of two conditions: first, that a midwife or another testifies to the birth from her, so the child is determined; second, that her husband confirms her, and she is married or in 'idda, claiming the child is from him, because it entails attributing lineage to the husband, so it is not binding by her statement alone, as lineage is by marriage bed and the right belongs to the husband, so if the husband confirms her, he has acknowledged it. But if she has no husband nor is in 'idda, or if she has a husband and claims the child is from someone else, her acknowledgment is valid because it imposes only on herself, not others, so it is enforced against her. (Al-Ayni, Al-Fath)
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage expands on two types of acknowledgment: acknowledgment of a master and a woman's acknowledgment of a child. For the master, whether he is the emancipator (mu'tiq) or the emancipated (mu'taq), the acknowledgment is valid as long as the right of wala' is not already established from another source. This is because it does not impose lineage on others. For a woman's acknowledgment of a child, the ruling depends on her marital status. If she is married or in 'idda and claims the child is from her husband, she must either have a midwife's testimony or her husband's confirmation to establish lineage; otherwise, the acknowledgment is not binding on the husband because lineage follows the marriage bed. However, if she has no husband or is not in 'idda, her acknowledgment alone suffices and is binding on her, as it only affects herself. Similarly, if she claims the child is from someone other than her husband, her acknowledgment is valid because it imposes solely on her. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that lineage attribution to others requires proof, while self-attribution does not.

Key Terms
مولى (mawlā): Master of emancipation (mu'tiq or mu'taq) in the context of wala' (patronage through emancipation).
قابلة (qābila): A midwife who testifies to the birth of a child from a woman, used as evidence for lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The woman's own statement alone.
B) Testimony of two male witnesses.
C) Confirmation by the husband or testimony of a midwife.
D) The child's acknowledgment.

Key Takeaway
A woman's acknowledgment of a child is valid, but when it imposes lineage on her husband, external proof (midwife or husband's confirmation) is required to protect his right.

Requirement of Confirmation and Ruling After Death
Intra-Hanafi dispute on confirmation after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general requirement of confirmation (tasdiq) in acknowledgments, identify the exceptions, and distinguish the Hanafi dispute regarding a husband's confirmation after the wife's death, applying the ruling to determine inheritance outcomes.

Core Idea
Confirmation after death is generally valid, but Abu Hanifa holds a husband's confirmation after his wife's death invalid because marriage ends completely.

Acknowledgment (iqrar) is a legal declaration that imposes rights, but it is not binding on the beneficiary unless they confirm it (tasdiq). However, this requirement is waived for minors and slaves. After the acknowledger dies, confirmation is normally valid because the right (like lineage or marital effects) persists. But there is a famous intra-Hanafi dispute: if a wife acknowledges a husband during her terminal illness, and the husband confirms only after her death, does it establish inheritance? Let's examine the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Sahibayn).

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and exceptions
Read the opening lines: confirmation is required from the acknowledged person (muqarr lahu) except if they are a minor or a slave of the acknowledger. Understand why exceptions exist (incapacity or ownership).
The general rule protects individuals from being bound by an acknowledgment they do not accept.
2
Understand the default permissibility after death
The text then says confirmation after the death of the acknowledger is generally valid because the right (e.g., lineage) continues. Note the examples given (inheritance, dower, washing the deceased).
3
Locate the specific dispute
Focus on the phrase 'Except the confirmation of the husband...' This is a special case where there is disagreement. Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa says invalid; the two disciples say valid.
4
Follow Abu Hanifa's argument
Abu Hanifa argues that the marriage is completely terminated by the wife's death: the husband can marry her sister and four others, and he cannot wash her. Therefore, her acknowledgment becomes void, and his subsequent confirmation cannot revive it.
He uses the consequences of death as evidence of complete dissolution.
5
Follow the Sahibayn's argument
The Sahibayn argue that the marriage remains for purposes of inheritance and acknowledgment; the husband never denied it, so his confirmation is valid, and he inherits from her. They also note that if he had brought evidence, it would be accepted.
They focus on the continuity of certain effects (inheritance) and the absence of denial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولابد من تصديق هؤلاء [يعني تصديق الولد والوالدين والزوجة والمولى والزوج. (عيني)] أي إنما يصح الإقرار إذا صدق المقر له في الإقرار في المسائل كلها؛ لأن إقرار غيرهم لا يلزمهم؛ لأن كلاً . منهم في يد نفسه إلا إذا كان المقر له صغيراً لا يعبر عن نفسه، أو عبداً له فيثبت نسبه بمجرد الإقرار، ولو كان عبداً لغيره يشترط تصديق مولاه. (عيني، فتح) وصح التصديق أي صح تصديق المقر له من هؤلاء المذكورين بعد موت المقر؛ لبقاء النسب بعد موت المقر، وإن أقر بنكاحها فصدقته بعد موته صح حتى يكون لها الميراث والمهر؛ لبقاء حكم النكاح، وهو العدة، فإنها آثار النكاح، ولهذا جاز لها غسله كما في حالة الحياة ميتاً. إلا تصديق الزوج إلخ: أي إذا أقرت المرأة بالزوج، فصدقها الزوج بعد موتها، فإنه لا يصح؛ لانقطاع النكاح بعد موت المرأة عند أبي حنيفة، وأما إذا أقر الزوج بالزوجة وصدقت المرأة بعد موت الزوج، فإنه لا تصح بالاتفاق، وعندهما يجوز تصديق الزوج بعد موت الزوجة؛ لبقاء النكاح بعد موت المرأة في حق الإرث والإقرار قائم؛ لأن التكذيب منه لم يوجد، فصح التصديق بعد موتها، فيثبت النكاح بتصادقهما، فيرث منها، ولهذا لو أقام البينة على النكاح بعد موتها، تقبل، وله: أنها لما ماتت زال النكاح بعلائقه، حتى يجوز له أن يتزوج أختها، وأربعا سواها، ولا يحل له أن يغسلها، فبطل إقرارها، فلا يصح التصديق بعد بطلان الإقرار والحاصل أنه فرق بين تصديق الزوج والزوجة، فإن تصديق الزوجة بعد موت الزوج، يصح بالاتفاق؛ لأن حكم النكاح باق في حقها، وإنما الخلاف في تصديق الزوج بعد موت الزوجة، فعند أبي حنيفة: لا يجوز، وعندهما يجوز فعليه مهرها وله الميراث منها. (عيني، فتح، زيلعي)
And confirmation of these is necessary – meaning confirmation of the child, parents, spouse, master, and husband. (Al-Ayni) That is, the acknowledgment is only valid if the acknowledged person confirms the acknowledgment in all cases, because the acknowledgment of others is not binding on them, since each is in control of himself, except if the acknowledged person is a minor who cannot express himself, or his own slave, then his lineage is established by the mere acknowledgment; but if it is another's slave, the confirmation of his master is required. (Al-Ayni, Al-Fath) And confirmation is valid – meaning the confirmation of the acknowledged person from these mentioned after the death of the acknowledging person is valid, because lineage continues after the death of the acknowledger. And if he acknowledges marriage to her and she confirms after his death, it is valid so that she gets inheritance and dower, because the ruling of marriage remains, which is the 'idda, for they are effects of marriage, and so it is permissible for her to wash him (for burial) as in life. Except the confirmation of the husband etc.: that is, if a woman acknowledges a husband and the husband confirms after her death, it is not valid because the marriage is terminated after the woman's death according to Abu Hanifa. But if the husband acknowledges a wife and the woman confirms after the husband's death, then it is not valid by consensus, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible for the husband to confirm after the wife's death, because the marriage remains after the woman's death in respect of inheritance and the acknowledgment is standing, since the denial (takdhib) from him did not occur, so the confirmation is valid after her death, thus the marriage is established by their mutual confirmation, so he inherits from her, and for this reason if he presents evidence of the marriage after her death, it is accepted. And for him (Abu Hanifa): because when she died, the marriage ceased with its attachments, so that it is permissible for him to marry her sister and four others besides her, and it is not permissible for him to wash her, so her acknowledgment is invalidated, and confirmation is not valid after the invalidation of the acknowledgment. The conclusion is that there is a difference between the confirmation of the husband and the wife: the wife's confirmation after the husband's death is valid by consensus, because the ruling of marriage remains in her favor; the dispute is only regarding the husband's confirmation after the wife's death. According to Abu Hanifa: it is not allowed; according to the two (Sahibayn): it is allowed, so he owes her dower and inherits from her. (Al-Ayni, Al-Fath, Zayla'i)
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage discusses two main points: first, the general requirement that the person in whose favor an acknowledgment is made (al-muqarr lahu) must confirm it, unless they are a minor or a slave of the acknowledger. This is because an acknowledgment imposes a right, and that right cannot be forced upon someone who does not accept it, except in cases of incapacity. Second, the ruling on confirmation after the death of the acknowledging person. The default is that confirmation after death is valid because the right (e.g., lineage or marital effects) may persist. However, there is a dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the husband's confirmation after the wife's death. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the husband's confirmation is not valid because marriage ends completely with the wife's death, allowing him to marry her sister and four others, and he cannot wash her. Thus, her acknowledgment during illness is voided, and his subsequent confirmation cannot revive it. According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the marriage's effects, such as inheritance, remain, so the husband's confirmation is valid, and he inherits from her. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that if the husband confirms after her death, under Abu Hanifa's view he does not inherit; under the Sahibayn's view he does. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in later fatwa is often that of Abu Hanifa due to his stronger analogy, but the passage presents the dispute.

Key Terms
تصديق (tasdiq): Confirmation by the acknowledged party that the acknowledgment is true, necessary for the acknowledgment to be binding on others.
موت المقر (mawt al-muqirr): Death of the person making the acknowledgment; confirmation may still be valid after this event because the right (e.g., lineage) remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is a husband's confirmation of his wife's acknowledgment of marriage after her death not valid?
A) Because the wife's acknowledgment was not valid from the start.
B) Because the marriage is completely terminated, so the acknowledgment is void.
C) Because the husband must confirm before death.
D) Because the wife's heirs must confirm.

Key Takeaway
Confirmation after death is valid unless the marriage is completely terminated, as per Abu Hanifa's view on husband's confirmation after wife's death.

Sick Person's Acknowledgment of Lineage: When Does It Affect Inheritance?
Ruling and commentary on acknowledging nasab affecting inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sick person's acknowledgment of lineage and distinguish when it establishes inheritance rights versus when it is treated as a will.

Core Idea
A sick person's acknowledgment of lineage does not establish nasab against others, but if no heir exists, it operates as a will for the entire estate.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between an acknowledgment that binds the declarant personally and one that imposes lineage on others. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explores when a sick person's claim of brotherhood or uncleanship entitles the claimant to inheritance. The key is whether there are any existing heirs: if not, the acknowledgment functions as a will; if there are, the claim fails unless confirmed by all heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sick person's acknowledgment of lineage (e.g., claiming another is his brother or paternal uncle). The general ruling is that such acknowledgment does not establish lineage for inheritance purposes against other heirs. However, if the sick person has no other heir at all, the acknowledged person inherits the entire estate.
2
Locate the key condition
The crucial condition is the presence or absence of any other heir. The text states: 'If he has no other heir, near or far, then the acknowledgee inherits.' If there is any heir (Quranic heir, agnate, or even distant relative like dhu al-arham), the acknowledgee does not inherit.
3
Analyze the legal mechanism
When no heir exists, the sick person can dispose of his entire property. Thus the acknowledgment effectively becomes a bequest (wasiyyah) for the whole estate. Since the deceased has no legal heirs, the estate passes to the acknowledgee as if by will, but subject to limits: if the sick person later makes another bequest, the acknowledgee only gets one-third without consent.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on husband's confirmation
A related issue: the husband's confirmation after the wife's death. Abu Hanifa rules it invalid because marriage ends with death; the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it valid because inheritance rights persist. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn.
The wife's confirmation after husband's death is valid by consensus.
5
Apply the analogy from the Hidayah
The passage compares to a buyer who acknowledges that the seller emancipated a purchased slave. The buyer's acknowledgment is accepted regarding the slave's freedom (affecting his own right) but not for reclaiming the price (affecting the seller). Similarly, the acknowledgment of lineage is valid regarding the acknowledger's own inheritance share but not for imposing nasab on other heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإقرار
أحكام إقرار المريض
وإن أقر بنسب نحو الأخ والعم لم يثبت فإن لم يكن له وارث غيره قريب أو بعيد أي رجل بأن قال لآخر هذا أخي نسبهما من الأب والجد المقر أي غير المقر له ورثه، وإن كان لا، ومن مات أبوه فأقر بأخ شركه في الإرث، ولم يثبت نسبه. أي شركه الأخ المقر فلا يصح التصديق بعد بطلان الإقرار والحاصل أنه فرق بين تصديق الزوج والزوجة، فإن تصديق الزوجة بعد موت الزوج، يصح بالاتفاق؛ لأن حكم النكاح باق في حقها، وإنما الخلاف في تصديق الزوج بعد موت الزوجة، فعند أبي حنيفة: لا يجوز، وعندهما يجوز فعليه مهرها وله الميراث منها. (عيني، فتح، زيلعي) وإن أقر إلخ: وكذا الجد وابن الابن فيما إذا أقر بابن الابن في حياة ابنه لم يثبت: أي نسب الأخ من الأب والعم من الجد؛ لأن فيه حمل النسب على غيره، فلا يجوز ما لم يصدقه المقر عليه والورثة وهم من أهل التصديق، أو أقام المقر البينة على ذلك، ويصح هذا الإقرار في حق نفسه، حتى تلزمه الأحكام من النفقة والحضانة والإرث إذا تصادقا على ذلك؛ لأن إقرارهما حجة عليهما. [رمز الحقائق: ۲۲۸/۲] فإن لم يكن له إلخ: مثل ملا مسكين للقريب بالعم، وللبعيد بمولى الموالاة، وعلق عليه في "فتح المعين": أن هذا موافق لما في "الزيلعي" حيث مثل للقريب بذوي الأرحام، وللبعيد بمولى الموالاة، ويخالفه ما صرح به في "العناية": من أن الوارث القريب كذوي الفروض والعصبات، والبعيد كذوي الأرحام، وقال في "الشرنبلالية" وما قاله الزيلعي أوجه؛ لأن مولى الموالاة إرثه بعد ذوي الأرحام مقدماً على المقر له بنسب الغير. انتهى. غيره قريب: كذوي الفروض والعصبات ورثه لأنه أقر بنسب على الغير فلا يقبل وباستحقاق ماله بعده، فيقبل حيث لا مزاحم؛ إذ له أن يتصرف في ماله بما شاء، فيوصي بجميعه، فيجعله لهذا المقر له، فهو وصية من عنه إرث من وجه فلم يرجع بأكثر وصيته من الثلث بدون إجازة المقر له ما دام على إقراره فلو أقر بأخ ثم أوصى لآخر بكل ماله، فله هذا الثلث، ولو عكس اشتركا. (حموي عن الكافي، فتح) وإن كان لا: أي إن كان له وارث لا يرث المقر له؛ لأن النسب لم يثبت بإقراره، فلا يستحق الميراث مع وارث معروف قريباً كان أو بعيداً [رمز الحقائق (۲۲۸/۲] ومن مات أبوه إلخ قيل: هذه المسألة بعينها فهمت مما تقدم، فتقع هذه مكررة، قلت: ليس كذلك؛ لأن المقر في المسألة السابقة مورث وههنا وارث، وإن كانتا سواء في عدم الثبوت [رمز الحقائق ۲۲۸/۲۲] شركه في الإرث أي شرك المقر له المقر في نصيبه من الإرث، فيستحق المقر له نصف نصيب المقر مطلقاً، فلو أقر بأخت تأخذ ثلث ما في يده، ولو أقر ابن وبنت بأخ وكذبهما ابن وبنت، يقسم نصيب المقرين أخماساً، ولو أقر بامرأة أنها زوجة أبيه، أخذت ثمن ما في يده. [البحر الرائق: ٣٦٤/٧] ولم يثبت نسبه إلخ أي شرك الأخ المقر له المقر في الإرث، لكن لم يثبت نسبه؛ لأن إقراره تضمن شيئين: حمل النسب على الغير، ولا ولاية عليه، والاشتراك في المال، وله فيه ولاية، فيثبت كالمشتري إذا أقر على البائع بعتق العبد المشتري، لم يقبل إقراره عليه حتى لا يرجع عليه بالثمن، ولكن يقبل في حق العتق حتى يعتق عليه ما اشتراه؛ لكونه إقرار على نفسه في حق ذلك. [هداية: ١٢٨/٦] وجه، فله أن تنفذ
Book of Acknowledgment. Rulings of a Sick Person's Acknowledgment. If he acknowledges lineage like brother or paternal uncle, it is not established. But if he has no other heir, near or far, meaning any person, by saying to another 'This is my brother, their lineage is from father and grandfather', the acknowledger (i.e., other than the acknowledgee) inherits from him. And if he has [an heir], then not. And one whose father died and he acknowledges a brother, he shares in the inheritance, but his lineage is not established. (i.e., the acknowledging brother shares [the acknowledgee] in inheritance.) So confirmation [by others] is not valid after the nullity of the acknowledgment. The conclusion is that there is a difference between the confirmation of the husband and the wife: the wife's confirmation after the husband's death is valid by agreement because the ruling of marriage remains in her right; the dispute is only about the husband's confirmation after the wife's death. According to Abu Hanifa: it is not permissible, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is permissible, so he pays her dower and inherits from her. (Ayni, Fath, Zaylai). 'And if he acknowledges etc.': Likewise the grandfather and the son's son when he acknowledges a son's son during the life of his son, it is not established: i.e., the lineage of a brother from the father and an uncle from the grandfather; because it involves imposing lineage on another, so it is not permissible unless the one upon whom it is acknowledged and the heirs confirm, and they are qualified to confirm, or the acknowledger provides evidence for that. This acknowledgment is valid regarding himself, so the rulings of maintenance, custody, and inheritance become binding on him if they mutually affirm it, because their acknowledgment is a proof against them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/228] 'If he has no other heir etc.': Such as Mulla Miskin gave the example of a near relative as an uncle, and a distant relative as a client of alliance (mawla al-muwalah). And it is commented in Fath al-Mu'in that this agrees with what is in al-Zaylai where he gave the example of a near relative as dhu al-arham, and a distant relative as mawla al-muwalah. But it contradicts what is stated in al-Inayah that the near heir is like the Quranic heirs and agnates, and the distant is like dhu al-arham. And he said in al-Sharnablaliyyah: What al-Zaylai said is more appropriate because the inheritance of mawla al-muwalah comes after dhu al-arham, preceding the acknowledgee of a foreign lineage. End. 'Other than a near relative': like the Quranic heirs and agnates, he inherits because he acknowledged a lineage upon another, so it is not accepted, and by the entitlement of his property after him, it is accepted where there is no competitor, since he may dispose of his property as he wishes, bequeath all of it, and give it to this acknowledgee. So it is a will from someone who is an heir in some respect, so it does not exceed more than one-third of his will without the permission of the acknowledgee as long as he persists in his acknowledgment. If he acknowledges a brother then bequeaths all his property to another, he gets that one-third. If reversed, they share. (Hamawi from al-Kafi, Fath). 'And if he has [an heir]': i.e., if he has an heir, the acknowledgee does not inherit, because lineage is not established by his acknowledgment, so he does not deserve inheritance with a known heir, near or far. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/228] 'And one whose father died etc.' It was said: This very issue is understood from what preceded, so this is repetitive. I say: It is not so, because the acknowledger in the previous issue is a testator, and here he is an heir, although both are similar in non-establishment. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/228] 'He shares in the inheritance': i.e., he makes the acknowledgee share with the acknowledger in his portion of inheritance, so the acknowledgee deserves half of the acknowledger's portion absolutely. If he acknowledges a sister, she takes one-third of what is in his hand. If a son and daughter acknowledge a brother and another son and daughter deny him, the portion of the acknowledgers is divided into fifths. If he acknowledges a woman as his father's wife, she takes one-eighth of what is in his hand. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 7/364] 'And his lineage is not established etc.': i.e., the acknowledging brother shares the acknowledgment with the acknowledger in inheritance, but his lineage is not established because his acknowledgment included two things: imposing lineage upon another, and he has no authority over that, and sharing in property, and he has authority over that. So it is established, like a buyer who acknowledges upon the seller the emancipation of the purchased slave—his acknowledgment is not accepted against him so that he cannot reclaim the price from him, but it is accepted regarding the emancipation so that his purchase becomes free, because it is an acknowledgment against himself in that respect. [Hidayah: 6/128] 'So he has the right to execute'.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Acknowledgment discusses the rulings of a sick person's acknowledgment of lineage (nasab). The first ruling: If a sick person acknowledges another as his brother or paternal uncle, this does not establish the lineage for inheritance purposes. However, if the sick person has no other heir at all—either near (like Quranic heirs and agnates) or distant (like dhu al-arham or a client of alliance)—then the acknowledged person inherits all the property. This is because the acknowledgment is effectively a will (wasiyyah) from the sick person, who can dispose of up to one-third of his property; but here since there is no heir, it operates as a bequest of the entire estate. If there is any heir, the acknowledged person does not inherit because lineage is not established. An important nuance: if the father dies and a son acknowledges a brother, the acknowledged brother shares the son's inheritance but lineage is still not established. The passage then distinguishes between a wife's confirmation after the husband's death (valid by consensus) and a husband's confirmation after the wife's death (disputed: Abu Hanifa disallows, the two companions allow). The commentary explains that the acknowledgment is valid regarding the acknowledger's own rights (like maintenance, custody, and inheritance if mutually affirmed) but not regarding others. The later discussion contrasts the views of Zaylai and Inayah on defining near and distant heirs. Finally, the passage draws an analogy to a buyer who acknowledges that the seller emancipated the purchased slave—the acknowledgment is accepted for the emancipation (affecting the buyer's own right) but not for claiming back the price.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Acknowledgment or admission of a right or fact, legally binding on the one who makes it.
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage or family connection, especially paternity.
المقر (al-muqirr): The person who makes the acknowledgment.
المقر له (al-muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor the acknowledgment is made.
التصديق (al-tasdiq): Confirmation or endorsement of an acknowledgment by a third party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a sick person acknowledges a brother and has no other heirs at all, the acknowledged brother inherits:
A) Only one-third of the estate.
B) The entire estate.
C) Nothing because lineage is not established.
D) Half of the estate because he is a brother.

Key Takeaway
A sick person's acknowledgment of lineage does not establish nasab against existing heirs but gives the acknowledged person the entire estate if there are no heirs, operating as a will.
