أحكام المكاتب

وإن كاتبه على خمر أو خنزير، أو قيمته المولى أي مال المكاتبة لأتلف المولى ما في يدها، فلم يحصل لها الغرض من الكتابة، ومنافع البضع ملحقة بالأجزاء، فيجب عليه عوضه، وهو العقر عند إتلافه بالوطء، نعم! لا حد ولا قود على المولى للشبهة، ولو وطئ مكاتبته مرارا فعليه مهر واحد؛ لأنه شبهة ملك، ولو شرط وطئها بأن كاتبها بألف على أن يطأها مدة الكتابة فسدت الكتابة، وتعتق بأداء لبدل، ولا يثبت لها شيء من الأحكام المتعلقة بما قبل الأداء. واعلم أن المولى يغرم في وطئ المكاتبة العقر، وفي لجناية عليها أو على ولدها الأرش، وفي إتلاف مالها المال، والمراد بالعقر في الإماء عشر قيمتها إن كانت بكرا، وإن كانت ثيبا فنصف عشر قيمتها فتح، تكملة بزيادة وتوضيح من المحشي.

وإن كاتبه على خمرٍ إلخ لما فرغ المصنف عن بيان الكتابة الصحيحة شرع في بيان الفاسدة؛ لأن الفاسدة تتلو لصحيحة، والمراد بالفاسدة هنا ما الباطلة كما ستعلم، وبين المصنف خمس صور من الكتابة الفاسدة، فالأول الثاني: أن يكاتب عبده على خمر أو خنزير، بيانهما على ما في "التكملة": أنه لو كاتب المسلم عبده المسلم أو الكافر في دار الإسلام على خمر أو خنزير، فالكتابة فاسدة؛ لأن الخمر والخنزير ليس بمال في حق المسلم، فلا يصلح عوضا، فيفسد العقد؛ لأن تسمية ما ليس بمتقوم في حق ما يحتاج فيه إلى تسمية البدل توجب فساد العقد كالبيع. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٨٤/٨] قال في "الفتح" على قول المصنف: "وإن كاتبه إلى آخره يعني لو كاتب المسلم عبده المسلم على حمر أو خنزير فالكتابة فاسدة وكذا إن كان المولى ذميا والعبد مسلما أو عكسه، قال لحموي: ويمكن إدخال الصور المذكورة في قوله وإن كاتبه إلخ، ولما صرح بعد بالصحة فيما إذا كانا كافرين علم عدم الصحة فيما عدا ذلك. انتهى وكذا في الرد المحتار" حيث قال: "أفاد أنه لو كان أحدهما مسلما لا يجوز للعلة المذكورة"، وإنما قيد بقوله: على خمر أو خنزير"؛ لأنه لو كاتبه على ميتة أو دم فالكتابة باطلة، فإن أدى لا يعتق إلا إذا قال: إن أديت إلي فيعتق لأجل اليمين لا لأجل الكتابة، قال في "التكملة: وإنما قيدنا بدار الإسلام؛ لأن المسلم الذي في دار الإسلام لو دخل دار الحرب فكاتب عبده المسلم أو الكافر على خمر أو خنزير فحكمه كما لو كاتب في دار الإسلام، أما لو أسلم في دار الحرب ولم تبلغه الأحكام، فكاتب على خمر أو خنزير، فالظاهر أنها صحيحة ويعتق بأداء ذلك انتهى باختصار، واعلم أن للمولى الفسخ في الكتابة بغير رضاء المكاتب وللمكاتب فسخها مطلقا في الجائزة والفاسدة وإن لم يرض المولى. ملتقط من الفتح والتكملة وغيرهما)

أو قيمته: هذه الصورة الثالثة من الصور الخمس بيانها أن يكاتب عبده على قيمته وهي فاسدة أيضا؛ لأن القيمة مجهولة القدر؛ لأنها تختلف باختلاف المقومين وجنسها كذلك مجهول، فصار كما لو كاتب على ثوب أو دابة؛ لأن الثوب والدابة أجناس مختلفة، وما هو مجهول الجنس لا يثبت في الذمة حتى في النكاح. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٨٥/٨] ثم إذا أدى قيمته عتق؛ لأنها هي البدل. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٢/٢] وهذا إذا تصادقا على مقدار، أما عند عدم التصادق لابد من أداء أقصى ما يقع به تقويم المقومين تكملة وعيني باختصار مع زيادة)

أو عين لغيره، أو مائة ليرد سيده وصيفا فسد، فإن أدى الخمر عتق .
كاتبه على مائة إلخ عقد الكتابة المكاتب معاوضة، أو عين لغيره: [ كاتبه على شيء عين لغيره] هذه هي الصورة الرابعة من الصور الخمس، بيانها: أن يكاتب عبده على أن يؤدي العبد شيئا معينا لغيره وهي فاسدة أيضا؛ لأنه لا يقدر على تسليمه، والقدرة على تسليم المعقود عليه شرط الصحة، والمراد به شيء يتعين بالتعيين كالثوب والعبد والمكيل والموزون غير النقدين، حتى لو كاتبه على دراهم أو دنانير بعينها وهي لغيره تجوز الكتابة؛ لأن النقود لا تتعين بالتعيين في العقود التي هي ولا في فسوخها، وإنما يجب مثلها في الذمة. واختلفوا في أنه إذا كاتبه على شيء معين لغيره هل يكون العقد باطلا أو فاسدا؟ ففي "الزيلعي" و"العناية": أنه إذا كاتبه على عين لغيره تتعين بالتعيين، لا ينعقد العقد أصلا في ظاهر الرواية إلا إذا قال: إذا أديت لي فأنت حر، فحينئذ يعتق بحكم الشرط، فهذا يفيد أنه باطل، وفي "القهستاني" معزيا لقاضي خان: الأظهر فيه الفساد كالمكيل والموزون والمذروع. كذا في الفتح بزيادة وتغيير)

أو مائة ليرد إلخ: هذه هي الصورة الخامسة بيانها: أنه إذا كاتبه على مائة دنانير على أن يرد المولى على المكاتب وصيفا أي عبدا للخدمة غير معين فسد العقد، وهذا عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف محله تجوز الكتابة، وتقسم المائة على قيمة وصيف وسط، فما أصاب الوصيف يسقط عنه، ويكون مكاتبا بما بقي؛ لأن كل ما جاز إيراد العقد عليه جاز استثناؤه منه وتجوز الكتابة على وصيف، فكذا يجوز استثناؤه، ولهما: أن بدل الكتابة مجهول القدر، فلا يصح كما إذا كاتبه على قيمة الوصيف؛ ولأنه عقد مشتمل على بيع وكتابة، فيبطل بجهالة الثمن والمثمن. رمز الحقائق: ۲۹۲/۲] وإنما قيدنا بقولنا: غير معين"؛ إذ لو كان معينا يجوز بالاتفاق؛ لجواز بيع المعين، فكذا استثناؤه.

واعلم أن هذه الكتابة باطلة ولهذا قلنا فيما قبل في حاشية قوله: "وإن كاتبه إلخ إن الفاسدة هنا تعم الباطلة، وذكر في "الفتح" عن "الشرنبلالية": أن هذه الكتابة باطلة أيضا بدليل ما في "الزيلعي" حيث قال: الأصل عند علمائنا الثلاثة: أن المسمى متى كان شيئا لا يصلح عوضا لجهالة القدر أو لجهالة الجنس، فإن العبد لا يعتق بأداء المسمى ولا بأداء القيمة؛ إذ لا ينعقد هذا العقد أصلا، ولهذا استشكل التعبير بالفساد . بطلان بعض الصور، ثم أجيب بأن المراد بالفاسد ما يعم الباطل كما في قولهم باب البيع الفاسد. (باختصار) وصيفا هو العبد للخدمة جمعه وصفاء. فسد متعلق بالصور الخمس أي فسد العقد في كل واحد من الصور، وقد بينا وجه كل واحد منها بتفصيل فتذكر. فإن أدى الخمر إلخ يعني إذا كاتبه على حمر أو خنزير، ثم أدى الخمر أو الخنزير قبل أن يبطل القاضي العقد عتق المكاتب وإن كان العقد فاسدا، سواء قال: إن أديتها فأنت حر، أو لا؛ لأنهما مال في الجملة وإن لم يكن لهما قيمة في حق المسلمين. وأما الميتة والدم فليسا بمال أصلا عند أحد، فلم ينعقد العقد بهما، فاعتبر فيهما معنى الشرط لا غير، وذلك بالتعليق صريحا، وهذا هو ظاهر الرواية، وفي المسألة اختلاف رواية عن الإمام، وخلاف زفر وأبي يوسف تركناه للاختصار، من أراد الإطلاع فلينظر في "العيني" وغيره. قال في "رد المحتار" عند قول المتن: "فإن أدى الخمر عتق" لم يبين حكم العتق في باقي الصور الفاسدة، وقدمنا أنه يعتق بأداء قيمته إذا كاتبه عليها؛ لأنها معلومة من وجه، وتصير معلومة.
Book of Kitab al-Mukatab: Rulings of the Mukatab. And if he makes a kitaba with him for wine or pork, or its value... the master causes loss to what is in her hand, so she does not achieve the purpose of kitaba, and the benefits of the vulva are attached to the parts, so he must pay compensation, which is the 'aqr when he destroys it by intercourse. Yes, there is no hadd or qisas on the master due to doubt. If he repeatedly has intercourse with his mukataba, he owes one mahr; because it is a doubt of ownership. If he stipulates intercourse by making kitaba with her for one thousand on condition that he has intercourse with her during the period of kitaba, the kitaba becomes invalid, and she becomes free upon payment of the substitute, and no ruling related to before payment is established for her. Know that the master pays the 'aqr for intercourse with the mukataba, and for injury upon her or her child the arsh, and for destruction of her property the property. The meaning of 'aqr for slave women is one-tenth of her value if she was a virgin, and if she was a non-virgin then half of one-tenth of her value. (Commentary: completion with addition and clarification from the marginal annotator.) And if he makes kitaba with him for wine etc. When the author finished explaining the valid kitaba, he began explaining the invalid one; because the invalid follows the valid, and what is meant by 'invalid' here is the 'batil' (void) as you will learn. The author explained five forms of invalid kitaba. The first and second: that he makes kitaba with his slave for wine or pork. Their explanation according to what is in 'al-Takmila': if a Muslim makes kitaba with his Muslim slave or a disbeliever in Dar al-Islam for wine or pork, the kitaba is invalid; because wine and pork are not property with respect to the Muslim, so they are not suitable as compensation, thus the contract becomes invalid; because naming something that is not valuable with respect to what needs naming of the substitute causes invalidity of the contract like sale. (from Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/84) He said in al-Fath on the author's statement: 'And if he makes kitaba with him...' meaning if a Muslim makes kitaba with his Muslim slave for wine or pork, the kitaba is invalid. Likewise if the master is a dhimmi and the slave is a Muslim, or vice versa. Al-Hamwi said: It is possible to include the mentioned forms in his statement 'and if he makes kitaba with him etc.' And when he explicitly stated later the validity when both are disbelievers, it is known that it is not valid in other than that. (End) Likewise in al-Radd al-Mukhtar where he said: 'He indicated that if either of them is Muslim, it is not permissible due to the mentioned cause.' He only restricted it with 'for wine or pork' because if he made kitaba with him for carrion or blood, the kitaba is void, and if he pays, he does not become free unless he said: 'If you pay it to me, you are free' then he becomes free due to the oath, not due to the kitaba. He said in al-Takmila: 'We only restricted it to Dar al-Islam because if a Muslim who is in Dar al-Islam enters Dar al-Harb and makes kitaba with his Muslim or disbeliever slave for wine or pork, its ruling is as if he made kitaba in Dar al-Islam. But if he became Muslim in Dar al-Harb and the rulings did not reach him, then he makes kitaba for wine or pork, the apparent view is that it is valid and he becomes free upon payment thereof.' (End summarized). And know that the master has the right to rescind the kitaba without the consent of the mukatab, and the mukatab has the right to rescind it absolutely in valid and invalid forms even if the master does not consent. (Selected from al-Fath, al-Takmila and others.) Or its value: This is the third form of the five forms. Its explanation: that he makes kitaba with his slave for his value, and it is also invalid; because the value is unknown in amount; because it varies among valuers, and its type is likewise unknown, so it becomes as if he made kitaba for a garment or an animal; because garments and animals are different types, and what is unknown in type cannot be established as a debt, even in marriage. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/85) Then if he pays its value, he becomes free; because it is the substitute. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/292) This is if they agree on the amount. But when they do not agree, he must pay the maximum valuation by the valuers. (Takmila and 'Ayni summarized with addition.) Or a specific item belonging to someone else, or one hundred in return for the master returning a servant: it is invalid. Then if he pays the wine, he becomes free. (Commentary on 'Or a specific item belonging to someone else': This is the fourth form of the five forms. Its explanation: that he makes kitaba with his slave that the slave shall pay a specific item belonging to someone else, and it is also invalid; because he is not able to deliver it, and ability to deliver the subject matter is a condition of validity. What is meant is something that is specified by specification, such as a garment, a slave, a measured or weighed item other than gold and silver. So if he makes kitaba with him for specific dirhams or dinars belonging to someone else, the kitaba is valid; because currencies are not specified by specification in contracts that are... nor in their rescissions, and only their like is due in the dhimmah. They differed whether when he makes kitaba with him for a specific item belonging to someone else, the contract is void or invalid. In al-Zayla'i and al-'Inaya: if he makes kitaba with him for a specific item belonging to someone else, it is specified by specification, the contract does not occur at all in the apparent narration unless he says: 'If you pay it to me, you are free' then he becomes free by virtue of the condition; this indicates it is void. And in al-Qahistani citing Qadi Khan: the more apparent is that it is invalid like measured, weighed, and length-measured items. (From al-Fath with addition and modification.) Or one hundred in return etc.: This is the fifth form. Its explanation: if he makes kitaba with him for one hundred dinars on condition that the master returns to the mukatab a servant (i.e. a slave for service) unspecified, the contract is invalid. This is according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, the kitaba is valid, and the one hundred is divided over the value of an average servant; whatever portion of the servant is dropped, and he becomes a mukatab for the remainder; because whatever is permissible to include in the contract is permissible to exclude from it, and kitaba for a servant is valid, so its exclusion is also valid. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the substitute in kitaba is unknown in amount, so it is not valid, as if he made kitaba with him for the value of the servant; and because it is a contract comprising a sale and a kitaba, so it becomes void due to ignorance of the price and the priced item. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/292) We only restricted it by saying 'unspecified'; because if it was specified, it is valid by agreement, due to the permissibility of selling a specified item, so likewise its exclusion. Know that this kitaba is void, and for this reason we said earlier in the gloss on his statement 'and if he makes kitaba with him etc.' that 'invalid' here encompasses 'void'. And it is mentioned in al-Fath from al-Sharnablaliyya that this kitaba is also void, as evidenced by what is in al-Zayla'i where he said: 'The principle with our three imams is that when the named thing is something that is not suitable as compensation due to ignorance of amount or ignorance of type, the slave does not become free by paying the named thing nor by paying the value; because this contract does not occur at all, and for this reason the expression 'invalid' was questioned. (Voidness of some forms, then it was answered that what is meant by 'invalid' is that which includes the void, as in their statement: 'Chapter of invalid sale.') (Summarized) 'Servant' is a slave for service; its plural is wusfaa'. 'Invalid' relates to the five forms, i.e. the contract is invalid in each one of the forms, and we have explained each one in detail, so remember. 'Then if he pays the wine etc.' means if he makes kitaba with him for wine or pork, then he pays the wine or pork before the judge annuls the contract, the mukatab becomes free even though the contract is invalid, whether he said: 'If you pay them, you are free' or not; because they are property in general even though they have no value with respect to Muslims. As for carrion and blood, they are not property at all according to anyone, so the contract is not concluded with them, so only the meaning of a condition is considered in them, and that is by explicit conditional statement. This is the apparent narration, and there is a difference of narration from the Imam on this issue, and the disagreement of Zafar and Abu Yusuf; we left it for brevity. Whoever wants to see it should look in al-'Ayni and others. He said in Radd al-Mukhtar at the author's statement: 'Then if he pays the wine, he becomes free' — he did not explain the ruling on emancipation in the remaining invalid forms, and we have already mentioned that he becomes free by paying its value if he made kitaba with him for it; because it is known in one respect and becomes known.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the five invalid forms of the kitaba (contract of manumission by payment). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, presents these forms after having discussed the valid kitaba. The commentary expands on each form with proofs and distinctions.

The first form: kitaba for wine or pork. The commentator explains that these are not considered property (mal) with respect to Muslims, so they cannot serve as valid compensation. The invalidity is analogized to a sale (qiyas 'ala al-bay'). The ruling applies when both parties are Muslim or one is Muslim in Dar al-Islam. If both are non-Muslims, the kitaba is valid according to the text. The commentator notes that if the consideration is carrion or blood, which are not property at all, the contract is void (batil) and not merely invalid (fasid).

The second form: kitaba for the slave's own value. This is invalid because the value is unknown in amount and type. The analogy is made to kitaba for a garment or animal, which are of different types and thus cannot be fixed as a debt. However, if the slave pays his value, he becomes free, but only if both agree on the amount; otherwise, the maximum valuation must be paid.

The third form: kitaba for a specific item belonging to someone else. The slave cannot deliver what he does not own, so the contract is invalid due to inability to deliver. An exception is made for dirhams and dinars, which are fungible and not specified in contracts. There is a difference of opinion whether such a contract is void (batil) or invalid (fasid). The commentator prefers the view that it is void.

The fourth form: kitaba for one hundred dirhams on condition that the master returns a servant (unspecified). This is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani because the substitute becomes unknown in amount. Abu Yusuf disagrees and considers it valid by analogy to valid contracts where a condition is permissible. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

The passage concludes by stating that despite the invalidity, if the slave actually pays the wine or pork before the judge annuls the contract, he becomes free. This is because wine and pork, while not valuable for Muslims, are still considered property in a general sense. This ruling does not apply to carrion or blood, which are not property at all. The commentator also notes that in the remaining invalid forms, emancipation occurs upon payment as well.

Key Terms
الكتابة الفاسدة (al-kitaba al-fasida): Invalid kitaba which, according to the commentator, includes both invalid (fasid) and void (batil) contracts, as per Hanafi usage.
المتقوم (al-mutaqawwim): Property that is valuable and permissible to trade (mal) in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason for the invalidity of kitaba for a specific item belonging to another person?
A) The item is not mal mutaqawwim
B) The item is unknown in amount
C) The slave cannot deliver it
D) The item is wine

Key Takeaway
The first four invalid kitaba forms fail because the consideration is either non-property, unknown, or undeliverable, mirroring the conditions for valid consideration in sale.

The Fifth Invalid Form: Dispute on Kitaba with a Condition to Return a Servant
Explaining the fifth invalid form of kitaba and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the nature of the intra-Hanafi dispute in the fifth form of kitaba and state the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Kitaba with a condition to return an unspecified servant is invalid due to unknown consideration, despite Abu Yusuf's valid alternative.

The fifth form of invalid kitaba involves a contract for one hundred dinars with the condition that the master returns an unspecified servant to the slave. This created a dispute between Abu Yusuf and the other two imams. Understanding the reasoning behind each view sharpens your ability to apply qiyas and recognize the scope of permissible conditions in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the precise terms of the contract
The master makes kitaba with the slave for 100 dinars on condition that the master returns a servant (unspecified) to the slave. The condition means the master owes a servant back.
The servant is not specified; it is a general 'servant for service' (wasif).
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They hold the kitaba is invalid because the substitute (badal) becomes unknown in amount (the servant's value is part of the consideration, but the servant is unspecified). They analogize it to kitaba for the value of a servant, which is also invalid due to ignorance.
They also argue the contract is a mix of sale and kitaba, invalid due to ignorance of price and priced item.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds the kitaba is valid. He argues that anything permissible to include in a contract is permissible to exclude. Since kitaba for a specified servant is valid, excluding that servant (i.e., condition that the master returns a servant) is also valid. He divides the 100 dinars: subtract the value of an average servant, and the slave is a mukatab for the remainder.
This is a form of partial kitaba, which is valid in Hanafi.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
The response is that the condition creates ignorance of the total consideration: the servant is unspecified, so its value is unknown, making the contract like kitaba for an unknown amount. Additionally, the contract combines a sale element (the servant) with kitaba, leading to more uncertainty.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
5
Apply the ruling: consequence of invalidity
Since the contract is invalid (batil), the slave does not become free by paying the 100 dinars alone. He would need to pay the full value of the servant as well, unless the contract is rectified. If the servant is specified, all agree it is valid.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Abu Yusuf's view would free the slave upon payment of 100 minus average servant's value; the majority view requires payment of the full 100 plus the servant's value (or rectification).

كتاب المكاتب
أحكام المكاتب

وإن كاتبه على خمر أو خنزير، أو قيمته المولى أي مال المكاتبة لأتلف المولى ما في يدها، فلم يحصل لها الغرض من الكتابة، ومنافع البضع ملحقة بالأجزاء، فيجب عليه عوضه، وهو العقر عند إتلافه بالوطء، نعم! لا حد ولا قود على المولى للشبهة، ولو وطئ مكاتبته مرارا فعليه مهر واحد؛ لأنه شبهة ملك، ولو شرط وطئها بأن كاتبها بألف على أن يطأها مدة الكتابة فسدت الكتابة، وتعتق بأداء لبدل، ولا يثبت لها شيء من الأحكام المتعلقة بما قبل الأداء. واعلم أن المولى يغرم في وطئ المكاتبة العقر، وفي لجناية عليها أو على ولدها الأرش، وفي إتلاف مالها المال، والمراد بالعقر في الإماء عشر قيمتها إن كانت بكرا، وإن كانت ثيبا فنصف عشر قيمتها فتح، تكملة بزيادة وتوضيح من المحشي.

وإن كاتبه على خمرٍ إلخ لما فرغ المصنف عن بيان الكتابة الصحيحة شرع في بيان الفاسدة؛ لأن الفاسدة تتلو لصحيحة، والمراد بالفاسدة هنا ما الباطلة كما ستعلم، وبين المصنف خمس صور من الكتابة الفاسدة، فالأول الثاني: أن يكاتب عبده على خمر أو خنزير، بيانهما على ما في "التكملة": أنه لو كاتب المسلم عبده المسلم أو الكافر في دار الإسلام على خمر أو خنزير، فالكتابة فاسدة؛ لأن الخمر والخنزير ليس بمال في حق المسلم، فلا يصلح عوضا، فيفسد العقد؛ لأن تسمية ما ليس بمتقوم في حق ما يحتاج فيه إلى تسمية البدل توجب فساد العقد كالبيع. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٨٤/٨] قال في "الفتح" على قول المصنف: "وإن كاتبه إلى آخره يعني لو كاتب المسلم عبده المسلم على حمر أو خنزير فالكتابة فاسدة وكذا إن كان المولى ذميا والعبد مسلما أو عكسه، قال لحموي: ويمكن إدخال الصور المذكورة في قوله وإن كاتبه إلخ، ولما صرح بعد بالصحة فيما إذا كانا كافرين علم عدم الصحة فيما عدا ذلك. انتهى وكذا في الرد المحتار" حيث قال: "أفاد أنه لو كان أحدهما مسلما لا يجوز للعلة المذكورة"، وإنما قيد بقوله: على خمر أو خنزير"؛ لأنه لو كاتبه على ميتة أو دم فالكتابة باطلة، فإن أدى لا يعتق إلا إذا قال: إن أديت إلي فيعتق لأجل اليمين لا لأجل الكتابة، قال في "التكملة: وإنما قيدنا بدار الإسلام؛ لأن المسلم الذي في دار الإسلام لو دخل دار الحرب فكاتب عبده المسلم أو الكافر على خمر أو خنزير فحكمه كما لو كاتب في دار الإسلام، أما لو أسلم في دار الحرب ولم تبلغه الأحكام، فكاتب على خمر أو خنزير، فالظاهر أنها صحيحة ويعتق بأداء ذلك انتهى باختصار، واعلم أن للمولى الفسخ في الكتابة بغير رضاء المكاتب وللمكاتب فسخها مطلقا في الجائزة والفاسدة وإن لم يرض المولى. ملتقط من الفتح والتكملة وغيرهما)

أو قيمته: هذه الصورة الثالثة من الصور الخمس بيانها أن يكاتب عبده على قيمته وهي فاسدة أيضا؛ لأن القيمة مجهولة القدر؛ لأنها تختلف باختلاف المقومين وجنسها كذلك مجهول، فصار كما لو كاتب على ثوب أو دابة؛ لأن الثوب والدابة أجناس مختلفة، وما هو مجهول الجنس لا يثبت في الذمة حتى في النكاح. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٨٥/٨] ثم إذا أدى قيمته عتق؛ لأنها هي البدل. [رمز الحقائق: ٢٩٢/٢] وهذا إذا تصادقا على مقدار، أما عند عدم التصادق لابد من أداء أقصى ما يقع به تقويم المقومين تكملة وعيني باختصار مع زيادة)

أو عين لغيره، أو مائة ليرد سيده وصيفا فسد، فإن أدى الخمر عتق .
كاتبه على مائة إلخ عقد الكتابة المكاتب معاوضة، أو عين لغيره: [ كاتبه على شيء عين لغيره] هذه هي الصورة الرابعة من الصور الخمس، بيانها: أن يكاتب عبده على أن يؤدي العبد شيئا معينا لغيره وهي فاسدة أيضا؛ لأنه لا يقدر على تسليمه، والقدرة على تسليم المعقود عليه شرط الصحة، والمراد به شيء يتعين بالتعيين كالثوب والعبد والمكيل والموزون غير النقدين، حتى لو كاتبه على دراهم أو دنانير بعينها وهي لغيره تجوز الكتابة؛ لأن النقود لا تتعين بالتعيين في العقود التي هي ولا في فسوخها، وإنما يجب مثلها في الذمة. واختلفوا في أنه إذا كاتبه على شيء معين لغيره هل يكون العقد باطلا أو فاسدا؟ ففي "الزيلعي" و"العناية": أنه إذا كاتبه على عين لغيره تتعين بالتعيين، لا ينعقد العقد أصلا في ظاهر الرواية إلا إذا قال: إذا أديت لي فأنت حر، فحينئذ يعتق بحكم الشرط، فهذا يفيد أنه باطل، وفي "القهستاني" معزيا لقاضي خان: الأظهر فيه الفساد كالمكيل والموزون والمذروع. كذا في الفتح بزيادة وتغيير)

أو مائة ليرد إلخ: هذه هي الصورة الخامسة بيانها: أنه إذا كاتبه على مائة دنانير على أن يرد المولى على المكاتب وصيفا أي عبدا للخدمة غير معين فسد العقد، وهذا عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف محله تجوز الكتابة، وتقسم المائة على قيمة وصيف وسط، فما أصاب الوصيف يسقط عنه، ويكون مكاتبا بما بقي؛ لأن كل ما جاز إيراد العقد عليه جاز استثناؤه منه وتجوز الكتابة على وصيف، فكذا يجوز استثناؤه، ولهما: أن بدل الكتابة مجهول القدر، فلا يصح كما إذا كاتبه على قيمة الوصيف؛ ولأنه عقد مشتمل على بيع وكتابة، فيبطل بجهالة الثمن والمثمن. رمز الحقائق: ۲۹۲/۲] وإنما قيدنا بقولنا: غير معين"؛ إذ لو كان معينا يجوز بالاتفاق؛ لجواز بيع المعين، فكذا استثناؤه.

واعلم أن هذه الكتابة باطلة ولهذا قلنا فيما قبل في حاشية قوله: "وإن كاتبه إلخ إن الفاسدة هنا تعم الباطلة، وذكر في "الفتح" عن "الشرنبلالية": أن هذه الكتابة باطلة أيضا بدليل ما في "الزيلعي" حيث قال: الأصل عند علمائنا الثلاثة: أن المسمى متى كان شيئا لا يصلح عوضا لجهالة القدر أو لجهالة الجنس، فإن العبد لا يعتق بأداء المسمى ولا بأداء القيمة؛ إذ لا ينعقد هذا العقد أصلا، ولهذا استشكل التعبير بالفساد . بطلان بعض الصور، ثم أجيب بأن المراد بالفاسد ما يعم الباطل كما في قولهم باب البيع الفاسد. (باختصار) وصيفا هو العبد للخدمة جمعه وصفاء. فسد متعلق بالصور الخمس أي فسد العقد في كل واحد من الصور، وقد بينا وجه كل واحد منها بتفصيل فتذكر. فإن أدى الخمر إلخ يعني إذا كاتبه على حمر أو خنزير، ثم أدى الخمر أو الخنزير قبل أن يبطل القاضي العقد عتق المكاتب وإن كان العقد فاسدا، سواء قال: إن أديتها فأنت حر، أو لا؛ لأنهما مال في الجملة وإن لم يكن لهما قيمة في حق المسلمين. وأما الميتة والدم فليسا بمال أصلا عند أحد، فلم ينعقد العقد بهما، فاعتبر فيهما معنى الشرط لا غير، وذلك بالتعليق صريحا، وهذا هو ظاهر الرواية، وفي المسألة اختلاف رواية عن الإمام، وخلاف زفر وأبي يوسف تركناه للاختصار، من أراد الإطلاع فلينظر في "العيني" وغيره. قال في "رد المحتار" عند قول المتن: "فإن أدى الخمر عتق" لم يبين حكم العتق في باقي الصور الفاسدة، وقدمنا أنه يعتق بأداء قيمته إذا كاتبه عليها؛ لأنها معلومة من وجه، وتصير معلومة.
Book of Kitab al-Mukatab: Rulings of the Mukatab. And if he makes a kitaba with him for wine or pork, or its value... the master causes loss to what is in her hand, so she does not achieve the purpose of kitaba, and the benefits of the vulva are attached to the parts, so he must pay compensation, which is the 'aqr when he destroys it by intercourse. Yes, there is no hadd or qisas on the master due to doubt. If he repeatedly has intercourse with his mukataba, he owes one mahr; because it is a doubt of ownership. If he stipulates intercourse by making kitaba with her for one thousand on condition that he has intercourse with her during the period of kitaba, the kitaba becomes invalid, and she becomes free upon payment of the substitute, and no ruling related to before payment is established for her. Know that the master pays the 'aqr for intercourse with the mukataba, and for injury upon her or her child the arsh, and for destruction of her property the property. The meaning of 'aqr for slave women is one-tenth of her value if she was a virgin, and if she was a non-virgin then half of one-tenth of her value. (Commentary: completion with addition and clarification from the marginal annotator.) And if he makes kitaba with him for wine etc. When the author finished explaining the valid kitaba, he began explaining the invalid one; because the invalid follows the valid, and what is meant by 'invalid' here is the 'batil' (void) as you will learn. The author explained five forms of invalid kitaba. The first and second: that he makes kitaba with his slave for wine or pork. Their explanation according to what is in 'al-Takmila': if a Muslim makes kitaba with his Muslim slave or a disbeliever in Dar al-Islam for wine or pork, the kitaba is invalid; because wine and pork are not property with respect to the Muslim, so they are not suitable as compensation, thus the contract becomes invalid; because naming something that is not valuable with respect to what needs naming of the substitute causes invalidity of the contract like sale. (from Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/84) He said in al-Fath on the author's statement: 'And if he makes kitaba with him...' meaning if a Muslim makes kitaba with his Muslim slave for wine or pork, the kitaba is invalid. Likewise if the master is a dhimmi and the slave is a Muslim, or vice versa. Al-Hamwi said: It is possible to include the mentioned forms in his statement 'and if he makes kitaba with him etc.' And when he explicitly stated later the validity when both are disbelievers, it is known that it is not valid in other than that. (End) Likewise in al-Radd al-Mukhtar where he said: 'He indicated that if either of them is Muslim, it is not permissible due to the mentioned cause.' He only restricted it with 'for wine or pork' because if he made kitaba with him for carrion or blood, the kitaba is void, and if he pays, he does not become free unless he said: 'If you pay it to me, you are free' then he becomes free due to the oath, not due to the kitaba. He said in al-Takmila: 'We only restricted it to Dar al-Islam because if a Muslim who is in Dar al-Islam enters Dar al-Harb and makes kitaba with his Muslim or disbeliever slave for wine or pork, its ruling is as if he made kitaba in Dar al-Islam. But if he became Muslim in Dar al-Harb and the rulings did not reach him, then he makes kitaba for wine or pork, the apparent view is that it is valid and he becomes free upon payment thereof.' (End summarized). And know that the master has the right to rescind the kitaba without the consent of the mukatab, and the mukatab has the right to rescind it absolutely in valid and invalid forms even if the master does not consent. (Selected from al-Fath, al-Takmila and others.) Or its value: This is the third form of the five forms. Its explanation: that he makes kitaba with his slave for his value, and it is also invalid; because the value is unknown in amount; because it varies among valuers, and its type is likewise unknown, so it becomes as if he made kitaba for a garment or an animal; because garments and animals are different types, and what is unknown in type cannot be established as a debt, even in marriage. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/85) Then if he pays its value, he becomes free; because it is the substitute. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/292) This is if they agree on the amount. But when they do not agree, he must pay the maximum valuation by the valuers. (Takmila and 'Ayni summarized with addition.) Or a specific item belonging to someone else, or one hundred in return for the master returning a servant: it is invalid. Then if he pays the wine, he becomes free. (Commentary on 'Or a specific item belonging to someone else': This is the fourth form of the five forms. Its explanation: that he makes kitaba with his slave that the slave shall pay a specific item belonging to someone else, and it is also invalid; because he is not able to deliver it, and ability to deliver the subject matter is a condition of validity. What is meant is something that is specified by specification, such as a garment, a slave, a measured or weighed item other than gold and silver. So if he makes kitaba with him for specific dirhams or dinars belonging to someone else, the kitaba is valid; because currencies are not specified by specification in contracts that are... nor in their rescissions, and only their like is due in the dhimmah. They differed whether when he makes kitaba with him for a specific item belonging to someone else, the contract is void or invalid. In al-Zayla'i and al-'Inaya: if he makes kitaba with him for a specific item belonging to someone else, it is specified by specification, the contract does not occur at all in the apparent narration unless he says: 'If you pay it to me, you are free' then he becomes free by virtue of the condition; this indicates it is void. And in al-Qahistani citing Qadi Khan: the more apparent is that it is invalid like measured, weighed, and length-measured items. (From al-Fath with addition and modification.) Or one hundred in return etc.: This is the fifth form. Its explanation: if he makes kitaba with him for one hundred dinars on condition that the master returns to the mukatab a servant (i.e. a slave for service) unspecified, the contract is invalid. This is according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, the kitaba is valid, and the one hundred is divided over the value of an average servant; whatever portion of the servant is dropped, and he becomes a mukatab for the remainder; because whatever is permissible to include in the contract is permissible to exclude from it, and kitaba for a servant is valid, so its exclusion is also valid. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the substitute in kitaba is unknown in amount, so it is not valid, as if he made kitaba with him for the value of the servant; and because it is a contract comprising a sale and a kitaba, so it becomes void due to ignorance of the price and the priced item. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2/292) We only restricted it by saying 'unspecified'; because if it was specified, it is valid by agreement, due to the permissibility of selling a specified item, so likewise its exclusion. Know that this kitaba is void, and for this reason we said earlier in the gloss on his statement 'and if he makes kitaba with him etc.' that 'invalid' here encompasses 'void'. And it is mentioned in al-Fath from al-Sharnablaliyya that this kitaba is also void, as evidenced by what is in al-Zayla'i where he said: 'The principle with our three imams is that when the named thing is something that is not suitable as compensation due to ignorance of amount or ignorance of type, the slave does not become free by paying the named thing nor by paying the value; because this contract does not occur at all, and for this reason the expression 'invalid' was questioned. (Voidness of some forms, then it was answered that what is meant by 'invalid' is that which includes the void, as in their statement: 'Chapter of invalid sale.') (Summarized) 'Servant' is a slave for service; its plural is wusfaa'. 'Invalid' relates to the five forms, i.e. the contract is invalid in each one of the forms, and we have explained each one in detail, so remember. 'Then if he pays the wine etc.' means if he makes kitaba with him for wine or pork, then he pays the wine or pork before the judge annuls the contract, the mukatab becomes free even though the contract is invalid, whether he said: 'If you pay them, you are free' or not; because they are property in general even though they have no value with respect to Muslims. As for carrion and blood, they are not property at all according to anyone, so the contract is not concluded with them, so only the meaning of a condition is considered in them, and that is by explicit conditional statement. This is the apparent narration, and there is a difference of narration from the Imam on this issue, and the disagreement of Zafar and Abu Yusuf; we left it for brevity. Whoever wants to see it should look in al-'Ayni and others. He said in Radd al-Mukhtar at the author's statement: 'Then if he pays the wine, he becomes free' — he did not explain the ruling on emancipation in the remaining invalid forms, and we have already mentioned that he becomes free by paying its value if he made kitaba with him for it; because it is known in one respect and becomes known.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the five invalid forms of the kitaba (contract of manumission by payment). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, presents these forms after having discussed the valid kitaba. The commentary expands on each form with proofs and distinctions.

The first form: kitaba for wine or pork. The commentator explains that these are not considered property (mal) with respect to Muslims, so they cannot serve as valid compensation. The invalidity is analogized to a sale (qiyas 'ala al-bay'). The ruling applies when both parties are Muslim or one is Muslim in Dar al-Islam. If both are non-Muslims, the kitaba is valid according to the text. The commentator notes that if the consideration is carrion or blood, which are not property at all, the contract is void (batil) and not merely invalid (fasid).

The second form: kitaba for the slave's own value. This is invalid because the value is unknown in amount and type. The analogy is made to kitaba for a garment or animal, which are of different types and thus cannot be fixed as a debt. However, if the slave pays his value, he becomes free, but only if both agree on the amount; otherwise, the maximum valuation must be paid.

The third form: kitaba for a specific item belonging to someone else. The slave cannot deliver what he does not own, so the contract is invalid due to inability to deliver. An exception is made for dirhams and dinars, which are fungible and not specified in contracts. There is a difference of opinion whether such a contract is void (batil) or invalid (fasid). The commentator prefers the view that it is void.

The fourth form: kitaba for one hundred dirhams on condition that the master returns a servant (unspecified). This is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani because the substitute becomes unknown in amount. Abu Yusuf disagrees and considers it valid by analogy to valid contracts where a condition is permissible. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

The passage concludes by stating that despite the invalidity, if the slave actually pays the wine or pork before the judge annuls the contract, he becomes free. This is because wine and pork, while not valuable for Muslims, are still considered property in a general sense. This ruling does not apply to carrion or blood, which are not property at all. The commentator also notes that in the remaining invalid forms, emancipation occurs upon payment as well.

Key Terms
الوصيف (al-wasif): A slave for service, not specified in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling regarding kitaba for 100 dinars with a condition that the master returns an unspecified servant?
A) Valid according to Abu Yusuf
B) Invalid due to ignorance of consideration
C) Valid if the slave agrees
D) Invalid only if the servant is not delivered

Key Takeaway
The fifth form of invalid kitaba involves a condition that introduces ignorance in the consideration; the relied-upon Hanafi view holds it invalid, despite Abu Yusuf's valid alternative.

Ruling on Mukatab Paying Kitabah with Wine
Explains the ruling when kitabah payment is wine and subsequent Islam of either party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a mukatab's kitabah payment is wine and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect on emancipation.

Core Idea
A kitabah contract on wine is valid, but upon Islam the master must take value; the mukatab is freed only upon paying the value.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a nuanced scenario: a mukatab (slave under a manumission contract) agrees to pay wine as kitabah. When either party embraces Islam, the ruling changes because Muslims cannot own or transfer wine. The commentators debate whether paying the wine itself still frees the slave or whether he must pay its cash value. Let us walk through the textual analysis and the internal Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Issue
Recognize that the kitabah contract specifies wine as the payment. The central question: what happens when one party becomes Muslim?
The contract is initially between two non-Muslims (or at least the slave is non-Muslim) because a Muslim cannot validly contract for wine.
2
Understand the Basis of Validity
The contract is valid because wine is considered property (mal) in the eyes of the contracting parties at the time of contract. This is a key Hanafi principle.
‘Māl’ includes anything of value, even if prohibited for consumption.
3
Trace the Effect of Islam
Once one party converts, the Muslim cannot receive or own wine. Therefore, the master (if Muslim) must take the value (price) of the wine, not the wine itself.
The value substitutes for the wine because the Muslim is prohibited from owning wine.
4
Distinguish Between the Two Positions
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Al-Naysaburi holds that if the slave actually pays the wine (even after Islam), he is freed because the contract specified it. Tahawi and Tamartashi hold that he is not freed; he must pay the value.
Both views derive from different interpretations of how the contract obligations change after Islam.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The text indicates that the relied-upon position (with ‘Allahu a’lam’) is that the slave is freed only upon paying the value, not the wine itself.
This tarjih is consistent with the principle that a Muslim cannot validly give or receive wine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على خمر وأيّ أسلم له قيمة الخمر، وعتق بقبضها. مقدار معلوم أي للمولى أي بقبض المولى قيمة الخمر. على خمر وصح هذا العقد أيضا؛ لأنه مال في حقهما. وأي أسلم إلخ أي وأي من المولى أو العبد أسلم فله أي للمولى قيمة الخمر؛ لأن المسلم ممنوع عن تمليكها ،وتملكها وهنا يلزم تمليك الخمر أو تملكها، فلا يجوز في حق المسلم، فيعجز عن تسليم الخمر، فوجب المصير إلى القيمة لقيامها مقام المسمى تكملة البحر الرائق: ۸۸/۸] وعتق إلخ : أي عتق العبد المذكور بقبضها أي قبض المولى قيمة الخمر؛ لأن الكتابة عقد معاوضة، وسلامة أحد العوضين لأحدهما سلامة العوض الآخر للآخر، وإن أدى الخمر عتق أيضا؛ لتضمن الكتابة تعليق العتق يوجب بأداء الخمر؛ إذ هي المذكورة في العقد، كذا في "شرح الجامع الصغير للنيسابوري، وفي "شرح الطحاوي" " والتمرتاشي" لو أدى الخمر لا يعتق، ولو أدى القيمة يعتق، والله أعلم.
On wine and whichever of them accepts Islam, he has the value of the wine, and he is freed upon its receipt. Known amount, meaning for the master, meaning by the master's receipt of the value of the wine. On wine, and this contract is also valid because it is property in their regard. And whichever accepts Islam, etc., meaning whichever of the master or the slave accepts Islam, he (the master) has the value of the wine because the Muslim is prohibited from giving ownership of it and owning it, and here it necessitates giving ownership of wine or owning it, so it is not permissible for the Muslim, so he becomes unable to deliver the wine, so it is necessary to resort to the value, as it stands in place of the named amount. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/88) And he is freed, etc.: meaning the mentioned slave is freed upon its receipt, i.e., the master's receipt of the value of the wine, because kitabah is a contract of exchange, and the soundness of one of the two counter-values for one party is the soundness of the other counter-value for the other. And if he pays the wine, he is also freed because kitabah entails the suspension of freedom upon paying the wine, since it is mentioned in the contract. This is in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Naysaburi. And in Sharh al-Tahawi and al-Tamartashi: if he pays the wine, he is not freed; if he pays the value, he is freed. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a mukatab (a slave with a manumission contract) has kitabah payment set as wine. The ruling: if either the master or the slave accepts Islam after the contract, the master is entitled to receive the value (price) of the wine, not the wine itself. This is because a Muslim cannot own or transfer wine. The slave is freed upon the master's receipt of that value. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to al-Naysaburi, if the slave actually pays the wine (despite the prohibition), he is still freed because the contract mentions it. However, according to al-Tahawi and al-Tamartashi, he is not freed by paying the wine; he must pay its value. The relied-upon position seems to be that he is freed only upon paying the value, as indicated by 'Allahu a'lam' at the end. The reasoning: kitabah is a contract of exchange, so the slave cannot unilaterally deliver an invalid item—he must give something of value.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in exchange for freedom.
الكتابة (al-kitabah): A contract of manumission where the slave pays a stipulated amount over time and becomes free upon completion.
القيمة (al-qima): The market value or price of the wine, which substitutes for the wine itself when the latter cannot be legally owned by a Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mukatab contracts on wine and then the master accepts Islam, what does the master receive?
A) The wine itself
B) The value of the wine
C) Nothing
D) The slave is freed without payment

Key Takeaway
In a kitabah contract on wine, if either party becomes Muslim, the master must receive the value of the wine, and the slave is freed only upon paying that value.

Permissible Financial Transactions for the Mukatab
Lists permissible transactions and explains the principle of financial independence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible financial transactions for a mukatab (slave under kitabah) and explain the scope of his authority to sell, including the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his students on excessive fraud (ghabn fahish).

Core Idea
The mukatab gains financial independence to earn his freedom; he may sell, buy, and travel, but Abu Hanifa allows excessive fraud while the Sahibayn restrict it.

In this lesson, we examine the financial independence that a mukatab acquires through a valid kitabah contract. The key principle is that the mukatab becomes 'free in hand' (yasir hurran yadan) — he can engage in transactions necessary to earn the money to pay off his kitabah. This includes selling, buying, traveling, and various other contracts. However, there is a notable intra-Hanafi difference regarding the extent of his authority to sell at a loss (ghabn fahish), which we will explore.

Guided Path
1
Understand the effect of valid kitabah
Recognize that a valid kitabah contract gives the mukatab a special legal capacity: he becomes 'free in hand' (hurr yadan), meaning he can own and dispose of property as needed to achieve freedom.
This is distinct from full freedom; the master retains ownership of the slave until the kitabah is paid off.
2
Identify the primary permissible transactions
The text lists: selling, buying, traveling, leasing, lending, deposit, acknowledgment of debt, collection, and acceptance of assignment of debt. Understand that these are all means to earn money.
Travel is permissible even if the master prohibits it, as it may be necessary for earning.
3
Analyze the authority to sell at different prices
The mukatab may sell at market price (thaman al-mithl), at a discount (mahabah), for cash or credit. He may also sell with moderate or excessive fraud (ghabn) according to Imam Abu Hanifa. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict excessive fraud, treating him like an authorized slave (abd ma'dhun).
The rationale for allowing discount is the custom of merchants to show leniency. The dispute on ghabn fahish is rooted in the extent of the mukatab's agency.
4
Apply the rulings to practical scenarios
Given a scenario, determine whether a mukatab may perform a specific transaction. For example, if a mukatab sells his master's property without permission, it is void. But if he sells his own acquired property, it is valid. Consider the ghabn issue: if he sells a valuable item for a fraction of its price, according to Abu Hanifa it is valid, but according to the Sahibayn it is not.
This distinction affects the validity of contracts and potential claims of fraud.

Source Text

Chapter on what is permissible for the mukatab to do or not do. Explanation: The mukatab may sell, purchase, travel, even if the master stipulated that he not leave the city, and marry off his slave woman. ... The mukatab. For the mukatab, because he benefits from the dowry. Chapter on what is permissible for the mukatab etc.: The author of al-'Inaya said: When he mentioned the rulings of valid and invalid kitabah, he began explaining what is permissible for the mukatab and what is not, for the permissibility of disposition is based on the valid contract. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/90) And know: In valid kitabah, the mukatab is established with rulings pertaining to kitabah, such as sale, purchase, and other dispositions before and after payment of the substitute. In invalid (fasid) kitabah, he does not have any of the rulings pertaining to before payment. In void (batil) kitabah, he does not have any rulings either before or after. So memorize that. For the mukatab etc. [Likewise, his leasing, lending, deposit, acknowledgment of debt, collection, and acceptance of assignment of debt upon him. (Fath)] Know that the basis of what the mukatab may do and what he may not do is that the effect of kitabah is that he becomes free in hand, that is, he possesses dispositions that lead to the goal, which is attaining freedom. Since selling, buying, and traveling are of this kind, it is permissible for him to sell, buy, and travel, because the master's goal in the contract is to obtain the substitute, and the slave's goal is to obtain freedom. This is achieved through selling and buying, and these may not coincide in residence, so he needs to travel, and the master may not prevent him. And when selling is permissible for him, he may sell at the market price, and at a discount (i.e., for a low price) because it is the custom of merchants to do so showing leniency and attracting people's hearts; and for cash or on credit; and with excessive or slight fraud according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not have the right to sell with excessive fraud, like the authorized slave. This is in the commentaries, summarized. Meaning: And even if he stipulates, etc.: [And according to Malik and al-Shafi'i in one opinion: he may not travel except with permission.] The 'in' here is connective, and this speech is connected to what preceded: he may travel even if the master stipulated that he not leave the city, just as if he specified a type of disposition for him to the exclusion of others, that is void, because it is a condition contrary to the requirement of the contract, which is ownership of hand. And the kitabah is not invalidated by such a condition because it is not in the substance of the contract. For an invalid condition only invalidates kitabah if it is embedded in the substance of the contract, that is, if it enters into one of the two counter-values, such as when he says: I contract with you for a thousand on condition that you serve me for a period of time. This is not like that, because it is a condition not in the substitute of kitabah nor in its equivalent, so the kitabah is not invalidated by it. The conclusion is that kitabah resembles sale in that it can be rescinded before payment of the substitute, and resembles marriage in that it cannot be rescinded after payment. Due to its resemblance to sale, it becomes invalid by a corrupt condition if it is embedded in the substance of the contract, such as being in the substitute, like stipulating his service, or contracting on wine or swine. (Takmila, Fath) And marriage of his slave woman: meaning the mukatab may marry off his slave woman, because it is a means of earning, so he has the right by necessity, unlike the marriage of the mukatabah herself, which is not permissible for her even though there is earning in it, because the master's ownership remains in her, and in marriage she is defective (i.e., her value decreases), and perhaps she becomes unable (to pay) and this defect remains, causing harm to the master. And her goal in marrying herself is not wealth, but rather protection and chastity, unlike the mukatab marrying off his slave woman, his slave woman:

Commentary
This chapter enumerates the actions that a mukatab (a slave under kitabah) is permitted to perform while still paying off his freedom. The key point is that the mukatab gains 'yad' (hand) meaning he becomes independent in financial matters to the extent needed to earn money to pay. He can sell, buy, travel even if the master forbids travel, because travel may be necessary for earning. He can also marry off his slave woman (if he owns one) to gain dowry. The text includes important details: The mukatab may sell at market price or at a discount, for cash or credit. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he can sell even with excessive fraud (ghabn fahish), but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict this like an authorized slave (abd ma'dhun). The master cannot restrict the mukatab's travel by stipulation in the contract; such a condition is invalid because it contradicts the purpose of kitabah. However, the condition does not invalidate the kitabah itself. The text compares kitabah to sale (can be revoked before payment) and to marriage (cannot be revoked after payment). There is also a note that according to Malik and al-Shafi'i, the mukatab cannot travel without permission. Finally, the permissibility for the mukatab to marry off his slave woman is distinguished from the case of a mukatabah marrying herself, which is not allowed due to potential harm to the master.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has a kitabah contract; he is partially free in financial matters.
اليد (al-yad): The legal capacity to own and dispose of property; the mukatab becomes 'free in hand' meaning he can engage in transactions.
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghabn al-fahish): Excessive fraud or disparity in price, where the difference is significant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mukatab's financial independence is broad and includes selling, buying, traveling, and leasing, but his authority to sell at a significant loss (ghabn fahish) is disputed within the Hanafi school.

Invalid Conditions in Kitabah and Marriage of the Mukatab's Slave Woman
Explains the effect of invalid conditions in kitabah and the permissibility of marriage arrangements involving the mukatab's slave woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a condition restricting a mukatab's travel is void and distinguish between the permissibility of a mukatab marrying off his slave woman versus a mukatabah marrying herself.

Core Idea
A condition in kitabah that contradicts its purpose is void but does not invalidate the contract; the mukatab may marry off his slave woman but a mukatabah may not marry herself.

This lesson continues from the previous one, focusing on two specific issues: (1) the legal effect of a condition in the kitabah contract that restricts the mukatab's travel, and (2) the ruling on the mukatab marrying off his slave woman. In both cases, the Hanafi school provides nuanced rulings that consider the purposes (maqasid) of the kitabah contract. We will also note the disagreement with Malik and al-Shafi'i on the travel condition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule on conditions in kitabah
Conditions that are embedded in the substance of the contract (i.e., in the counter-values) can invalidate the kitabah if they are invalid. Conditions external to the counter-values do not invalidate the contract, but they are themselves void.
Embedded in substance means the condition is part of the price or the service, e.g., 'I contract with you on condition you serve me.'
2
Apply to the travel restriction
The condition 'do not travel' is not part of the price or the substitute; it is an external stipulation. Since it contradicts the purpose of kitabah (enabling earning), it is void. However, the kitabah remains valid.
The passage analogizes: if a master specifies a specific type of disposition (e.g., only trade in cloth), that too is void.
3
Compare with the opposing school's view
Malik and al-Shafi'i (in one opinion) hold that the travel restriction is valid, and the mukatab cannot travel without permission. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
The Hanafi position is more permissive to help the mukatab earn.
4
Analyze the marriage of the mukatab's slave woman
The mukatab may marry off his slave woman because it is a means of earning (dowry) and he owns her. In contrast, a mukatabah (female mukatab) may not marry herself off because it causes harm to the master (defect in value) and her goal is not earning.
The distinction is based on ownership and purpose.

Explanation: The mukatab may sell, purchase, travel, even if the master stipulated that he not leave the city, and marry off his slave woman. ... The mukatab. For the mukatab, because he benefits from the dowry. Chapter on what is permissible for the mukatab etc.: The author of al-'Inaya said: When he mentioned the rulings of valid and invalid kitabah, he began explaining what is permissible for the mukatab and what is not, for the permissibility of disposition is based on the valid contract. (Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8/90) And know: In valid kitabah, the mukatab is established with rulings pertaining to kitabah, such as sale, purchase, and other dispositions before and after payment of the substitute. In invalid (fasid) kitabah, he does not have any of the rulings pertaining to before payment. In void (batil) kitabah, he does not have any rulings either before or after. So memorize that. For the mukatab etc. [Likewise, his leasing, lending, deposit, acknowledgment of debt, collection, and acceptance of assignment of debt upon him. (Fath)] Know that the basis of what the mukatab may do and what he may not do is that the effect of kitabah is that he becomes free in hand, that is, he possesses dispositions that lead to the goal, which is attaining freedom. Since selling, buying, and traveling are of this kind, it is permissible for him to sell, buy, and travel, because the master's goal in the contract is to obtain the substitute, and the slave's goal is to obtain freedom. This is achieved through selling and buying, and these may not coincide in residence, so he needs to travel, and the master may not prevent him. And when selling is permissible for him, he may sell at the market price, and at a discount (i.e., for a low price) because it is the custom of merchants to do so showing leniency and attracting people's hearts; and for cash or on credit; and with excessive or slight fraud according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not have the right to sell with excessive fraud, like the authorized slave. This is in the commentaries, summarized. Meaning: And even if he stipulates, etc.: [And according to Malik and al-Shafi'i in one opinion: he may not travel except with permission.] The 'in' here is connective, and this speech is connected to what preceded: he may travel even if the master stipulated that he not leave the city, just as if he specified a type of disposition for him to the exclusion of others, that is void, because it is a condition contrary to the requirement of the contract, which is ownership of hand. And the kitabah is not invalidated by such a condition because it is not in the substance of the contract. For an invalid condition only invalidates kitabah if it is embedded in the substance of the contract, that is, if it enters into one of the two counter-values, such as when he says: I contract with you for a thousand on condition that you serve me for a period of time. This is not like that, because it is a condition not in the substitute of kitabah nor in its equivalent, so the kitabah is not invalidated by it. The conclusion is that kitabah resembles sale in that it can be rescinded before payment of the substitute, and resembles marriage in that it cannot be rescinded after payment. Due to its resemblance to sale, it becomes invalid by a corrupt condition if it is embedded in the substance of the contract, such as being in the substitute, like stipulating his service, or contracting on wine or swine. (Takmila, Fath) And marriage of his slave woman: meaning the mukatab may marry off his slave woman, because it is a means of earning, so he has the right by necessity, unlike the marriage of the mukatabah herself, which is not permissible for her even though there is earning in it, because the master's ownership remains in her, and in marriage she is defective (i.e., her value decreases), and perhaps she becomes unable (to pay) and this defect remains, causing harm to the master. And her goal in marrying herself is not wealth, but rather protection and chastity, unlike the mukatab marrying off his slave woman, his slave woman:
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This chapter enumerates the actions that a mukatab (a slave under kitabah) is permitted to perform while still paying off his freedom. The key point is that the mukatab gains 'yad' (hand) meaning he becomes independent in financial matters to the extent needed to earn money to pay. He can sell, buy, travel even if the master forbids travel, because travel may be necessary for earning. He can also marry off his slave woman (if he owns one) to gain dowry. The text includes important details: The mukatab may sell at market price or at a discount, for cash or credit. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he can sell even with excessive fraud (ghabn fahish), but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict this like an authorized slave (abd ma'dhun). The master cannot restrict the mukatab's travel by stipulation in the contract; such a condition is invalid because it contradicts the purpose of kitabah. However, the condition does not invalidate the kitabah itself. The text compares kitabah to sale (can be revoked before payment) and to marriage (cannot be revoked after payment). There is also a note that according to Malik and al-Shafi'i, the mukatab cannot travel without permission. Finally, the permissibility for the mukatab to marry off his slave woman is distinguished from the case of a mukatabah marrying herself, which is not allowed due to potential harm to the master.

Key Terms
صلب العقد (sulb al-'aqd): The substance or core of the contract; specifically the counter-values (the price and the item/service being exchanged).
المكاتبة (al-mukatabah): A female slave under a kitabah contract.
تعيبها (ta'yibuha): The defect or decrease in value a female slave suffers upon marriage (due to loss of virginity or change in status).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, if a master stipulates in a kitabah contract that the mukatab cannot travel, what is the effect on the kitabah?
A) The condition is valid and the kitabah is valid; the mukatab cannot travel.
B) The condition is void, but the kitabah remains valid; the mukatab may travel.
C) The condition is void, and the kitabah becomes invalid.
D) The condition is valid only if both parties agree.

Key Takeaway
Conditions in kitabah that contradict its purpose but are not part of the core exchange are void yet do not invalidate the contract; the mukatab retains his rights, including the ability to travel and marry off his slave woman.

The Mukatab's Capacity to Trade and Travel
States basic permissibility and effect of restrictive conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mukatab may engage in trade and travel, and explain why a master's stipulation against travel is invalid but does not void the kitabah contract.

Core Idea
A mukatab may trade and travel freely; a condition restricting him is void but does not invalidate the kitabah.

This lesson explores the foundational principle that a mukatab (slave under kitabah) is permitted to conduct trade and travel because these actions are essential for earning the money to secure his freedom. We will also examine the effect of restrictive conditions imposed by the master, such as a stipulation not to leave the city. According to the Hanafi school, such conditions are invalid but do not nullify the kitabah contract itself, whereas other schools like Malik and al-Shafi'i hold a different view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State that the mukatab is permitted to sell, buy, and travel. The basis is that the kitabah grants him 'ownership of hand' (malikiyyat al-yad), enabling him to perform transactions that lead to freedom.
2
Analyze the master's restrictive condition
Understand that a condition preventing travel contradicts the contract's purpose. Since it is not embedded in the core contract (the two equivalents), it is void but the kitabah remains valid.
The condition does not invalidate the contract because it is not part of the consideration.
3
Compare with opposing school
Note that Malik and al-Shafi'i (in one opinion) hold that the mukatab cannot travel without the master's permission, showing a practical difference.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Chapter on what the mukatab may or may not do. Explanation: The mukatab may sell, buy, travel, even if he stipulated that he should not leave the city, and marry off his slave girl... The mukatab. The kitabah is not invalidated by such a condition because it is not in the core of the contract. A void condition only invalidates kitabah if it is embedded in the core of the contract, i.e., if it enters into one of the two equivalents, as when he says, 'I have made a kitabah with you for one thousand on condition that you serve me for a period of time.' That is not like this, because it is a condition not on the equivalent of kitabah nor on its counterpart, so the kitabah is not invalidated. The conclusion is that kitabah resembles sale in that it may be rescinded before payment of the equivalent, and it resembles marriage in that it may not be rescinded after payment. Due to its resemblance to sale, it is invalidated by a void condition if it is embedded in the core of the contract, i.e., in the equivalent, such as stipulating service or making a kitabah on a donkey or pig. (Takmila, Fath)
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary by al-Babarti et al. establishes the general principle that a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) is permitted to engage in trade and travel because these actions are necessary for him to earn the money to pay off his kitabah. The master's purpose is to receive the payment; the slave's purpose is to attain freedom. Therefore, any condition that restricts this—such as a stipulation not to leave the city—is invalid because it contradicts the very nature of the contract (malikiyyah al-yad). However, such a condition does not void the contract itself because it is not embedded in the core of the contract (i.e., it is not part of the two equivalents). The passage also clarifies that the mukatab may sell even at a loss (ghaban fahish) according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict this. The later part discusses the nature of kitabah: it is like a sale insofar as it can be rescinded before payment, and like marriage after payment.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah with his master to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum.
كتابة (kitābah): A contract between a master and slave whereby the slave is granted permission to work and earn money to pay for his freedom.
مالكية اليد (mālikiyyat al-yad): Ownership of hand, meaning the mukatab has the legal capacity to engage in transactions that lead to earning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a mukatab travel if his master stipulated that he not leave the city?
A) No, because the master's condition is valid and must be obeyed.
B) Yes, because the condition is invalid but the contract remains valid.
C) Yes, but only with the master's permission.
D) No, because travel is not considered necessary for earning.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab may trade and travel freely; a condition restricting these is invalid but does not nullify the kitabah contract.

The Mukatab's Sale Authority and the Nature of Kitabah
Expands on sale authority and nature of kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare Abu Hanifa and the two companions on ghaban fahish, and explain why kitabah resembles both sale and marriage in terms of rescission.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits the mukatab to sell at an excessive loss; the two companions forbid it. Kitabah is like sale before payment, like marriage after.

This lesson delves into the scope of the mukatab's authority to sell, specifically addressing whether he may sell at a price significantly below market value (ghaban fahish). We also explore the dual nature of the kitabah contract: it resembles a sale in that it can be rescinded before payment, and a marriage in that it becomes irrevocable after payment. Understanding these analogies clarifies many rulings on conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on sale pricing
State that the mukatab may sell at a fair price or at a discount, and according to Abu Hanifa even at an excessive loss (ghaban fahish). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) prohibit excessive loss, comparing him to an authorized slave (al-'abd al-ma'dhun).
The difference is based on whether the mukatab is viewed as having full ownership of hand or limited capacity.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Understand the qiyas: Abu Hanifa considers the mukatab's need to earn; the two companions equate him with an authorized slave who cannot sell at a loss.
The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated but the passage seems to favor Abu Hanifa's view.
3
Understand the dual nature of kitabah
Kitabah is analogous to sale (can be rescinded before payment) and to marriage (cannot be rescinded after payment). This affects how void conditions impact the contract.
A void condition in the core invalidates the kitabah due to its resemblance to sale.

باب ما يجوز للمكاتب أن يفعله أو لا يفعله في بيان للمكاتب البيع والشراء والسفر، وإن شرط أن لا يخرج من المصر، وتزويج أمته .. المكاتب . للمكاتب لأنه يستفيد به المهر باب ما يجوز للمكاتب إلخ : قال صاحب "العناية": لما ذكر أحكام الكتابة الصحيحة والفاسدة شرع في بيان ما يجوز للمكاتب وما لا يجوز، فإن جواز التصرف يبتني على العقد الصحيح تكملة البحر الرائق: ٩٠/٨] واعلم في الكتابة الصحيحة تثبت للمكاتب الأحكام المتعلقة بالكتابة من البيع والشراء وغير ذلك من التصرفات قبل أداء البدل وبعده، وفي الفاسدة لا يثبت له شيء من الأحكام المتعلقة بما قبل الأداء، وفي الباطلة لا يثبت له شيء من الأحكام لا قبله ولا بعده، فاحفظه. للمكاتب إلخ [وكذا إجارته وإعارته وإيداعه وإقراره بالدين واستيفاؤه وقبول حوالة بدين عليه. (تكملة، فتح)
Chapter on what the mukatab may or may not do. Explanation: The mukatab may sell, buy, travel, even if he stipulated that he should not leave the city, and marry off his slave girl... The mukatab. For the mukatab because he benefits from the dower. The author of al-'Inayah said: When he mentioned the rulings of valid and invalid kitabah, he began to explain what the mukatab may and may not do, because permissibility of transactions is based on the valid contract. [From Takmilat al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:90] Know that in a valid kitabah, the mukatab acquires rulings related to kitabah such as selling, buying, and other transactions before and after payment of the equivalent; in an invalid one, he does not acquire any rulings related to before payment; in a void one, he does not acquire any rulings either before or after. So memorize it. [The mukatab also has] hiring, lending, deposit, acknowledgment of debt, collection, acceptance of assignment of debt. (Fath) Know that the basis of what the mukatab may do and what he may not do is that the effect of kitabah is that he becomes free in hand (yad), i.e., he owns the transactions that lead to the goal, which is attaining freedom. Since selling, buying, and travel are of this kind, he is permitted to sell, buy, and travel, because the master's purpose in the contract is to receive the equivalent, and the slave's purpose is to attain freedom, and that is achieved through selling and buying. These may not be possible in the city, so he needs to travel, and the master may not prevent him. When he is permitted to sell, he may sell at a fair price, at a discount (i.e., a low price) because it is the custom of merchants to do so as a show of leniency and to attract people's hearts, for cash and credit, with excessive and slight loss (ghaban) according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), but according to the two companions, he may not sell with excessive loss, like the authorized slave. Thus in the commentaries, summarized. Explanation of 'even if he stipulated': [According to Malik and al-Shafi'i in one opinion: he may not travel without permission.] 'إن' here is wasliyyah, and this speech is connected to what preceded: he may travel even if his master stipulated that he not leave the city, just as if he specified a type of transaction for him without others, that condition is void because it contradicts the requirement of the contract, which is ownership of hand (malikiyyah al-yad). The kitabah is not invalidated by such a condition because it is not in the core of the contract. A void condition only invalidates kitabah if it is embedded in the core of the contract, i.e., if it enters into one of the two equivalents, as when he says, 'I have made a kitabah with you for one thousand on condition that you serve me for a period of time.' That is not like this, because it is a condition not on the equivalent of kitabah nor on its counterpart, so the kitabah is not invalidated. The conclusion is that kitabah resembles sale in that it may be rescinded before payment of the equivalent, and it resembles marriage in that it may not be rescinded after payment. Due to its resemblance to sale, it is invalidated by a void condition if it is embedded in the core of the contract, i.e., in the equivalent, such as stipulating service or making a kitabah on a donkey or pig. (Takmila, Fath)
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary by al-Babarti et al. establishes the general principle that a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) is permitted to engage in trade and travel because these actions are necessary for him to earn the money to pay off his kitabah. The master's purpose is to receive the payment; the slave's purpose is to attain freedom. Therefore, any condition that restricts this—such as a stipulation not to leave the city—is invalid because it contradicts the very nature of the contract (malikiyyah al-yad). However, such a condition does not void the contract itself because it is not embedded in the core of the contract (i.e., it is not part of the two equivalents). The passage also clarifies that the mukatab may sell even at a loss (ghaban fahish) according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict this. The later part discusses the nature of kitabah: it is like a sale insofar as it can be rescinded before payment, and like marriage after payment.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghaban fāḥish): Excessive loss in a sale, i.e., selling at a price significantly below market value.
عبد مأذون له (al-'abd al-ma'dhun lahu): A slave who has been given permission by his master to engage in trade, but with limited capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, can a mukatab sell his goods at a price significantly below market value?
A) No, because it harms the master's interest.
B) Yes, because the mukatab has the same capacity as an authorized slave.
C) Yes, because the mukatab needs to earn his freedom and such sales are customary.
D) No, because the mukatab is not permitted to sell at all.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa permits the mukatab to sell at an excessive loss, unlike the two companions; the kitabah contract is like a sale before payment and like marriage after.
